Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Contracts Not Invalidated by Invalid Conditions
Explains that certain contracts remain valid despite invalid conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that certain contracts are not invalidated by invalid conditions and apply it to at least three types of contracts (kafalah, hawalah, wakalah).

Core Idea
Invalid conditions do not void the contract; the condition is null and the contract stands.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym expands on a key Hanafi principle: many contracts remain valid despite containing invalid conditions. This may seem counterintuitive, but the school distinguishes between conditions that go to the core of the contract and those that are extraneous. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying rulings in sales, suretyship, and other transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The core principle: contracts are not invalidated by invalid conditions. The condition is void and the contract remains valid, as long as the condition does not affect the core (sulb) of the contract.
This applies to contracts that are not inherently dependent on the condition.
2
Distinguish Between Ta'liq and Shart
Suspending a contract (ta'liq) on a condition is different from appending an invalid condition (shart fasid). In some contracts (like iqalah), ta'liq is invalid, while an invalid condition does not spoil the contract.
This nuance is crucial for correctly classifying the scenario.
3
Examine the Examples
Work through each example: kafalah (suretyship), hawalah (transfer of debt), wakalah (agency), iqalah (rescission), kitabah (contract of manumission), idhn al-'abd (permission to trade), da'wat al-walad (claiming paternity), sulh (settlement), 'aqd al-dhimmah (dhimma contract), ta'liq al-radd bi al-'ayb (suspending return due to defect), khiyar al-shart (option of condition). For each, note that the contract is valid and the condition is void.
Some conditions (e.g., 'until the wind blows') are clearly invalid; the contract remains valid.
4
Identify the Exception
If the invalid condition is part of the core contract (sulb al-'aqd), such as stipulating a prohibited price (e.g., wine in kitabah), the contract itself becomes invalid.
This exception confirms the rule: external conditions do not invalidate, but internal ones do.
5
Understand the School's Consistency
The ruling is consistent across Hanafi sources (zahir al-riwayah). Some scholars like al-Nasafi and al-Marghinani affirm this principle, and it is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position for fatwa.
Cross-madhab differences exist; the Shafi'i school may rule differently in some cases.

And suretyship until the wind blows is valid and the condition is void. And al-Nasafi stated that if the condition is not customary, the suretyship is valid and the condition is void. And transfer of debt is like it. His statement: (And transfer of debt by his saying: I have transferred you to so-and-so on condition that you do not recourse upon me when he defaults; mentioned by al-'Ayni. Meaning the transfer is valid and the condition is void, so he recourses upon him when he defaults. And suspending it by a condition is valid, and from it is stipulating the option for the transferee, and it is permissible as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Then know that the transfer is invalidated by some conditions according to al-Bazzaziyyah. And among the forms of invalid transfer is when it is stipulated in the transfer that the transferee gives the transferred money to the transferee from the price of the house of the transferor because he is unable to fulfill the commitment, unlike if the transferee committed to give from the price of his own house because he is able to sell and is not forced to sell his house, as if its acceptance was conditional on payment at harvest time, he is not forced to pay before the term. End. And these apply to the absolute statement of the author and others. His statement: (And agency by his saying: I appoint you agent if you discharge me from what you have against me; mentioned by al-'Ayni. And it is an example of suspending it by a condition. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Suspending agency by a condition is valid, and suspending dismissal by it is invalid. And derived from that is his saying: Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent, because it is suspending appointment by dismissal, and the method of his dismissal will come. And if he said: Whenever I appoint you, you are dismissed, it is not valid because it is suspending dismissal by a condition. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Agency is not invalidated by invalid conditions, whatever condition it may be. And it has preceded that if they rescind for less than the first price or for another type, it does not become invalid and the first price is obligatory. And it is an example that it is not invalidated by invalid conditions. And as for what was mentioned, it is an example of suspending it. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Stipulating an option in it is permissible. Correct. His statement: (And the contract of manumission by his saying: I have contracted manumission with you for one thousand on condition that you do not leave the town, or stipulating the option for the transferee, whether that is from suspension; there is consideration, rather it is a condition but it is valid, not from our subject. Consider. His statement: (And these apply to the absolute statement of the author and others. He said in al-Nahr: Its answer is that this is a promise from the transferee and the discussion is not about it. End. And his meaning by the transferee is the one transferred to because its connection may be dropped. And this answer is not apparent because being a promise does not remove it from being a condition. His statement: (And as for what was mentioned) i.e., from the statement of al-'Ayni: I rescind the sale if you lend me. And the author's intent is to object to al-'Ayni that the intent is to explain what is not invalidated by an invalid condition, and what he mentioned as an example is suspension by a condition, and suspension by a condition is not valid as mentioned in al-Qunyah. And the author mentioned at the end of the chapter on rescission that the benefit of rescission being revocation appears in five issues: the second of them is that it is not invalidated by invalid conditions, but suspending it by a condition is not valid, such as if he sold an ox to Zayd and said: I bought it cheaply, so Zayd said: If you find a buyer at an increase, sell it to him, so he found and sold at an increase, the second sale is not concluded because it is suspending rescission, not agency. Book of sales, chapter of miscellaneous matters 317: trade, claiming the child, settlement for the blood of a slave, and for injury, and the dhimma contract, and suspending the return due to defect, and dismissal of the judge, and by the option of condition. He trades on condition that he does not deal with so-and-so or on condition that he works in a type of trade, then the contract of manumission on this condition is valid and the condition is void, so he may leave the town and do whatever he wants of types of trade with any person he wants, because the condition is not part of the core contract. But if it is part of the core contract, such as if it is in the price itself like the contract of manumission for wine and the like, then it becomes invalid by it as known in its place; mentioned by al-'Ayni. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He made a contract of manumission with her while she was pregnant on condition that her child enters the contract, it is invalid because it is invalidated by the invalid condition. His statement: (And permission for the slave to trade by his saying to his slave: I have permitted you to trade for up to a month or on condition that you trade in such-and-such, then his permission is general in trades and times and the condition is void. His statement: (And claiming the child by his saying to his slave-girl who gave birth to this child from me: If my wife is pleased with that. His statement: (And settlement for intentional blood by the guardian of the intentionally killed person making a settlement with the killer on something with the condition that he lends him or gives him a gift, then the settlement is valid and the condition is void, and the blood is dropped because it is among the renunciations and does not admit conditions. His statement: (And for injury) by making a settlement for it with the condition of lending something or giving a gift. His statement: (And the dhimma contract) by the imam saying to the harbi who seeks the dhimma contract: I have imposed on you the jizya if so-and-so wills, for example, then the dhimma contract is valid and the condition is void. His statement: (And suspending the return due to defect) by his saying: If I find a defect in the sold item, I return it to you if so-and-so wills, for example. His statement: (And by the option of condition) i.e., and suspending the return by the condition; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. End. His statement: (And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He made a contract of manumission with her while she was pregnant) contradicts what was presented from al-'Ayni, and what is in al-'Imadiyyah and al-Ustruwushniyyah agrees with him that suspending the contract of manumission by a condition is not permissible, and it is only invalidated by an invalid condition, but it was interpreted in al-Durar as the invalidity being in the core contract, evidenced by their second statement: The contract of manumission with a customary and non-customary condition is valid and the condition is void, for it is interpreted as when it is not in the core contract. And this reconciliation refutes the author of Jami' al-Fusulayn. Consider. Then on this basis, the contract of manumission should have been counted in the first section as well. His statement: (By his saying to his slave-girl who gave birth, etc.) There is that this is from suspension and the discussion is not about it, and similarly in al-Nahr: By his saying to his slave-girl after she gave birth to this child from me: Conditioned on the pleasure of my wife. End. And similarly in al-Durar: By the master saying: If this slave-girl has a pregnancy, it is from me. He said in al-'Azmiyyah: That this condition is invalid is a point for reflection. And he illustrated it in Idah al-Kirmani by claiming the lineage of twins on condition that the lineage of the other is not from him, or claiming the lineage of a child on condition that he does not inherit from him; the lineage of each of the twins is established and he inherits, and the condition is void because they are from one water, so necessarily the establishment of one's lineage necessitates the other's as known, and the condition that he does not inherit is an invalid condition due to its contradiction of the Shariah, and lineage is not invalidated by it. End. And what he illustrated in al-Durar was refuted in al-Shurunbulaliyyah also as will come shortly. His statement: (By his saying: If I find a defect in the sold item, I return it to you if so-and-so wills) There is that this is from suspension, so he should have said: on condition that so-and-so is pleased. There remains something here: the discussion is about what is not invalidated by an invalid condition, and suspending the return has been counted among them.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the principle that certain contracts are not invalidated by the inclusion of an invalid condition (shart fasid). The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains the rule and provides numerous examples, while also engaging with opinions of other scholars. The overall rule: if a contract is valid in its essence, an appended invalid condition does not nullify the contract; the condition itself is void and the contract stands. This applies to contracts that are not inherently dependent on the condition. The passage begins by contrasting pure conditions (which are already covered elsewhere) and then lists several contracts. For each, the commentator clarifies the ruling and sometimes discusses nuances, such as when the condition is part of the core contract (fi sarb al-'aqd) vs. external. The contracts covered include: 1) Kafalah (suretyship): a condition like 'until the wind blows' is void but the suretyship is valid. 2) Hawalah (transfer of debt): a condition that the creditor cannot recourse upon the transferor is void; the transfer stands. 3) Wakalah (agency): suspending agency by a condition is valid; suspending dismissal is invalid. 4) Iqalah (rescission): suspending rescission by a condition is invalid, but an invalid condition in the rescission itself does not nullify it. 5) Kitabah (contract of manumission): conditions about leaving town or trade are void, but the contract valid unless the condition is in the price. 6) Idhn al-'abd (permission for slave to trade): general permission stands; restrictive conditions void. 7) Da'wat al-walad (claiming paternity): a condition that the wife must be pleased is void; lineage is established. 8) Sulh 'an dam al-'amd (settlement for intentional killing): condition of loan/gift void; settlement valid. 9) Sulh 'an al-jarahah (settlement for injury): similar. 10) 'Aqd al-dhimmah (dhimma contract): condition of someone's permission void. 11) Ta'liq al-radd bi al-'ayb (suspending return due to defect): condition void, return valid. 12) Khiyar al-shart (option of condition): similar. The commentator also addresses discrepancies between sources, reconciling or critiquing other scholars' views. The core lesson: the validity of the contract depends on its own pillars, not on extraneous conditions.

Key Terms
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is invalid according to Shariah, such as a condition that contradicts the contract's nature or is not customary.
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta'liq bi al-shart): Suspending the contract or a legal effect on the occurrence of a future condition. Some contracts allow it; others do not.
صلب العقد (sulb al-'aqd): The core of the contract; the essential elements without which the contract cannot exist. Conditions that enter the core may invalidate it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person makes a contract of suretyship (kafalah) with the condition that the surety is only liable until the wind blows, what is the ruling?
A) The suretyship is invalid because the condition is invalid.
B) The suretyship is valid and the condition is binding.
C) The suretyship is valid but the condition is void.
D) The suretyship is suspended until the wind blows.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that many contracts remain valid despite containing invalid conditions; the condition itself is void and the contract stands.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Validity of Conditional Rescission and Dismissal of Judge
Author defends validity of conditional rescission and dismissal; commentator lists suspendable acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional rescission/dismissal and identify which acts can be suspended by condition according to the commentator.

Core Idea
A void condition does not invalidate non-financial acts like rescission or dismissal, but not all acts can be suspended by condition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key Hanafi principle: when a condition is attached to an act that is not a financial transaction, the act remains valid even if the condition is void. The author uses the examples of rescinding a sale using the option of condition and the caliph's dismissal of a judge. The commentator then expands on which specific types of acts can be validly suspended by condition, critiquing the original author for omissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the condition's effect
Read the initial ruling: when a person with khiyar al-shart says 'I return the sale if so-and-so wills,' or when the caliph dismisses a judge with a condition, what is the outcome? The passage states the rescission/dismissal is valid but the condition is void.
Remember the key phrase: يصح ويبطل الشرط (valid but the condition is void).
2
Understand the rationale
The author gives the reason: these acts are not financial transactions (mu'awada maliyya), so a void condition does not affect them. Think about why financial transactions are treated differently (e.g., gharar principle).
This is a qiyas-based proof: analogy to the principle that void conditions only invalidate financial contracts.
3
Analyze the commentator's expansion
The commentator lists acts that can be validly suspended: pure waivers (like divorce and manumission), obligations (like hajj and prayer), and appointments (like judgeship and emirate). He also notes what was omitted: permission in trade, handing over preemption, pledge, and the act of becoming Muslim. Note that gift can be suspended with a suitable condition.
The category 'isqatat mahda' (pure waivers) is central. Acts not involving financial exchange are generally safe.

بأن قال من له خيار الشرط في البيع رددت البيع أو قال أسقطت خياري إن شاء فلان فإنه يصح ويبطل الشرط قوله : ( وعزل القاضي بأن قال الخليفة للقاضي عزلتك عن القضاء إن شاء فلان فإنه ينعزل ويبطل الشرط لما ذكرنا أن هذه الأشياء ليست بمعاوضه مالية فلا يؤثر الشرط الفاسد . ولم يذكر المصنف رحمه الله تعالى ما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط . قال الشارح رحمه الله تعالى : إنه مختص بالإسقاطات المحضة التي يحلف بها كالطلاق والعتاق وبالالتزامات التي يحلف بها كالحج والصلاة والتوليات كالقضاء والامارة اهـ. وقد فاته الإذن في التجارة فإنه يصح تعليقه بالشرط كما في الخانية لكونه من الاسقاطات لكن لا يحلف به، فلو حذف التي يحلف بها لدخل ولدخل تعليق تسليم الشفعة فإن صحيح كما في البزازية لكونه إسقاطاً لكن لا يحلف به. وقد فات المصنف الرهن فإنه مما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد كما في البزازية وفاته أيضاً مسئلة الإسلام فإنه لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط كما في فتاوى قارئ الهداية. ويرد عليه أن الهبة يجوز تعليقها بالشرط الملائم نحو وهبتك على أن تقرضني كذا
That he who has the option of condition in sale said: I return the sale, or said: I have dropped my option if so-and-so wills, then it is valid and the condition is void. His statement: (and the dismissal of the judge when the caliph says to the judge: I dismiss you from the judiciary if so-and-so wills, then he is dismissed and the condition is void, because we mentioned that these are not financial transactions, so a void condition does not affect it. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, did not mention what may be suspended by condition. The commentator, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It is specific to pure waivers that are sworn by, like divorce and manumission, and to obligations that are sworn by, like hajj and prayer, and appointments like judgeship and emirate. And he missed permission in trade, for its suspension by condition is valid as in al-Khaniyya because it is from the waivers, but it is not sworn by. If he had deleted 'that are sworn by', it would include it, and it would include the suspension of handing over preemption, for it is valid as in al-Bazzaziyya because it is a waiver, but not sworn by. And the author missed pledge, for it is not invalidated by a void condition as in al-Bazzaziyya, and he also missed the matter of Islam, for its suspension by condition is not valid as in the fatawa of Qari' al-Hidaya. And it is objected to that gift can be suspended by a suitable condition, like: I give you provided that you lend me such-and-such.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author discusses the ruling on conditional rescission of a sale and conditional dismissal of a judge. He states that when a person with the option of condition (khiyar al-shart) says 'I return the sale' or 'I drop my option' conditional upon the will of another person (e.g., 'if so-and-so wills'), the rescission or waiver is valid, but the condition itself is void. Similarly, if the caliph dismisses a judge with a condition ('if so-and-so wills'), the dismissal is valid but the condition is void. The rationale is that these are not financial transactions (mu'awada maliyya), so a void condition does not nullify them. The commentator then notes that the original author (al-Mawsili) did not list what can be validly suspended by a condition. The commentator specifies: it applies only to pure waivers (isqatat mahda) that are sworn by, like divorce (talaq) and manumission ('itaq), and to obligations sworn by, like hajj and prayer, and appointments like judgeship and emirate. He criticizes the author for omitting permission in trade (idhn fi al-tijara), which is a valid suspension because it is a waiver, though not sworn by. He also omitted handing over preemption (taslim al-shuf'a), which is valid because it is a waiver. Pledge (rahn) is not invalidated by a void condition, and Islam (the act of becoming Muslim) cannot be suspended by condition. Finally, the commentator notes that gift (hiba) can be suspended by a suitable condition like 'I give you provided that you lend me such-and-such.'

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation in a sale, where the buyer or seller has the right to rescind within a specified period.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is void in Islamic law, e.g., a condition that contradicts the purpose of the contract.
إسقاط محض (isqat mahd): A pure waiver of a right, not involving any consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, which of the following acts CANNOT be suspended by a condition?
A) Divorce (talaq)
B) Manumission ('itaq)
C) Becoming Muslim (islam)
D) Handing over preemption (taslim al-shuf'a)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, void conditions attached to non-financial acts are themselves void, but the underlying act remains valid, and only certain acts can be validly suspended by condition.

Acts Valid for Suspension by Condition: The Commentator's Additions and Corrections
Critical commentary on classification of acts that can be suspended by a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which acts can be validly suspended by a condition according to the Hanafi school and explain the commentator's refinements to the earlier classification.

Core Idea
Suspension by condition is valid for pure cancellations and obligations, but the commentator expands it to include permission for trade and surrender of pre-emption, while excluding Islam.

The original author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not explicitly list all acts that can be validly suspended by a condition. The commentator in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides an initial classification and then points out several omissions and corrections. This lesson examines the refined Hanafi position on ta'liq (suspension), including the key distinction between acts that are sworn by and those that are not, and the special rules for mortgage and gift.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial classification
Identify the commentator's original statement: suspension is valid for pure cancellations (isqatat mahdah) like divorce and manumission, obligations like hajj and prayer, and appointments like judgeship and emirate.
These are acts that are commonly sworn by (yuhalafu biha).
2
Recognize the omissions
The commentator notes that the author missed permission for trade and surrender of pre-emption. Both are cancellations (isqat) but are not sworn by, so they should be included if the phrase 'which are sworn by' is omitted.
These are still valid for suspension even though one does not swear by them.
3
Analyze the mortgage and Islam exceptions
Mortgage (rahn) is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so it can be suspended. Islam cannot be suspended at all; its suspension is invalid.
This is based on later fatwa collections like al-Bazaziyya and Fatawa Qari' al-Hidaya.
4
Address the gift objection
Some might object that gift (hiba) cannot be suspended, but the commentator clarifies that gift can be suspended with a suitable condition (shart mula'im), such as 'I give you this on condition that you lend me such-and-such'.
This is from al-Durar and one of two opinions; the commentator leans toward validity.
5
Synthesize the refined classification
After adding the omitted acts and considering the exceptions, the Hanafi position on valid suspension includes: pure cancellations (whether sworn by or not), obligations, appointments, mortgage (with corrupt condition not invalidating), and gift (with suitable condition). It excludes Islam.
This refined list is the operative ruling in later Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Sales, Chapter of Miscellaneous: In it are corrupt conditions. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention what can be suspended by a condition. The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is specific to pure cancellations which are sworn by, such as divorce and manumission, and to obligations which are sworn by, such as hajj and prayer, and to appointments such as judgship and emirate. End. And he missed permission for trade, for its suspension by a condition is valid as in al-Khaniyya because it is from cancellations, but it is not sworn by. So if he omitted 'which are sworn by', it would include, and would include the suspension of surrender of pre-emption, for it is valid as in al-Bazaziyya because it is a cancellation, but it is not sworn by. And the author missed mortgage, for it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition as in al-Bazaziyya. And he also missed the issue of Islam, for its suspension by a condition is not valid as in the Fatawa of Qari' al-Hidaya. And it is objected to him that gift can be suspended by a suitable condition, such as 'I give you (this) on condition that you lend me such-and-such'; due to al-Durar for one of the two opinions, and the figures of al-Ayni are valid by suspension, and the objection against him and against the author is repelled, so reflect.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator (the author of al-Bahr) on his earlier classification. He begins by noting that the original author did not explicitly list what acts can be validly suspended by a condition. The commentator had previously said that suspension is limited to pure cancellations (like divorce and manumission) that are sworn by, obligations (like hajj and prayer) that are sworn by, and appointments (like judgship and emirate). He then points out that the author missed including permission for trade, which can be suspended according to al-Khaniyya because it is a cancellation, though it is not sworn by. He also notes that if the phrase 'which are sworn by' were removed, it would include surrender of pre-emption, which is also a cancellation and valid to suspend. Additionally, the author missed mortgage, which is not invalidated by a corrupt condition. And he missed the issue of Islam, which cannot be validly suspended according to Fatawa Qari' al-Hidaya. Finally, the commentator addresses an objection regarding gift: gift can be suspended by a suitable condition, like 'I give you this on condition that you lend me such-and-such', based on al-Durar for one opinion, and the objections are repelled. The passage encourages careful reflection.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal effect upon a future condition; here, making a contract or disposition conditional upon something.
إسقاط (isqat): A legal act of dropping or canceling a right; pure cancellations include divorce, manumission, surrender of pre-emption.
شرط فاسد (shart fāsid): A condition that is corrupt (invalid) in a contract, e.g., a condition that contravenes the contract's purpose.
شرط ملائم (shart mulā'im): A suitable condition that aligns with the contract's purpose, e.g., giving a gift on condition of receiving a loan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The commentator expanded the validity of suspension by condition to include any pure cancellation or obligation, regardless of being sworn by, and clarified that mortgage and gift (with suitable condition) are included, but Islam is not.

Validity of Suspending Surrender of Pre-emption: Pure Cancellation Debate
Detailed analysis of whether surrender of pre-emption is a pure cancellation and its suspension by condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the debate within the Hanafi school regarding whether surrender of pre-emption (تسليم الشفعة) is a pure cancellation (إسقاط محض) and evaluate the implications for suspending it by condition.

Core Idea
Surrender of pre-emption is not a pure cancellation—coercion affects it, unlike other pure cancellations.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi debate about the nature of surrendering the right of pre-emption. At its core is the question of whether this surrender is a pure cancellation (إسقاط محض) that can be suspended by a condition, similar to divorce or manumission. The discussion reveals a conflict between early authorities like al-Bazaziyya and later scholars such as al-Sarakhsi, with practical consequences for when and how a pre-emptor may waive his right.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling from al-Bazaziyya
First, note the view from al-Bazaziyya: suspending the cancellation of pre-emption by condition is permissible because it is a pure cancellation. Identify the key statement that 'it is a cancellation and a cancellation permits suspension.'
2
Examine the author's own application
The author (Ibn Nujaym) applies this to a scenario where the pre-emptor says before sale: 'If you buy, I have surrendered.' He notes that this is a suspension of cancellation before obligation, and per the rules of pure cancellations, it should be valid.
3
Introduce the opposing view from al-Dhahiriyya
Al-Dhahiriyya agrees that surrender can be suspended, but they raise an objection from al-Sarakhsi: if surrender were a pure cancellation, coercion would not affect it (as with other pure cancellations). Since coercion does invalidate surrender, it cannot be a pure cancellation.
This is the crucial counter-argument.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If it is a pure cancellation, suspension is valid even before the right arises; if not, suspension may be invalid. The author leans toward the latter, but admits he lacks an explicit text.
5
Synthesize the debate
The passage does not settle the issue definitively. It highlights the internal Hanafi disagreement and the method of testing a 'pure cancellation' by examining the effect of coercion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يذكر المصنف ما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط) أي لم يصرح به وإلا فأغلب ما قدمه مما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط كما نبهنا عليه سابقاً قوله : (ولدخل تعليق تسليم الشفعة الخ قال الرملي : عبارة البزازية في الشفعة تعليق إبطالها بالشرط جائز حتى لو قال سلمتها إن كنت اشتريتها لنفسك، فإن كان اشتراه لغيره لا تبطل لأنه إسقاط والإسقاط يحمل التعليق .اهـ. أقول : فلو قال الشفيع قبل البيع لمن يريد الشراء إن اشتريت فقد سلمتها هل يصح أم لا ولا شبهة أنه تعليق الإسقاط قبل الوجوب بوجود سببه . ومقتضى قولهم التعليق بالشرط المحض يجوز فيما كان من باب الإسقاط المحض، وقولهم المعلق بالشرط كالمنجز عند وجوده وقولهم من لا يملك التنجيز لا يملك التعليق إلا إذا علقه بالملك أو سببه صحة التعليق المذكور لأنه من باب الإسقاط وكأنه نجزه عند وجوده وقد علقه الملك فتأمل. لكن في الظهيرية ما هو صريح في أنه ليس إسقاطاً محضاً قال الظهيرية في الفتاوى الصغرى : تعليق إبطال الشفعة بالشرط جائز حتى لو قال سلمت لك شفعة هذه الدار إن كنت اشتريت لنفسك، فإن كان اشتراها لغيره كان الشفيع على شفعته لأن تسليم الشفعة إسقاط محض فيصح تعليقه بالشرط، لكن يرد على هذه مسألة إشكالاً وهو ما ذكره شمس الأئمة السرخسي في باب الصلح من الجنايات وكتاب الصلح من المبسوط أن القصاص لا تعليق إسقاطه بالشرط يصح ولا يحتمل الإضافة إلى الوقت وإن كان إسقاطاً محضاً، ولهذا لا يرتد برد من عليه القصاص، ولو أكره على إسقاط الشفعة فأسقط لا يبطل حقه في الشفعة. وبهذا تبين أن تسليم الشفعة ليس بإسقاط محض لأنه لو كان إسقاطاً لصح مع الإكراه اعتباراً بعامة الإسقاطات والمسألة في إكراه المبسوط اهـ. التعليق قبل الشراء كما لا يصح التنجيز قبله ولم أر من صرح بالمسألة مع أنها تقع كثيراً لكن الذي يظهر عدم صحة التعليق فيها، وأسأل الله تعالى الظفر بها في كلامهم فهو الموفق والمعين اهـ.
His saying: (And the author did not mention what can be suspended by a condition) i.e., he did not explicitly state it, otherwise most of what he presented is from what can be suspended by a condition as we pointed out earlier. His saying: (And it would include the suspension of surrender of pre-emption etc.) al-Ramli said: The wording of al-Bazaziyya on pre-emption: Suspension of its cancellation by a condition is permissible, even if he says 'I have surrendered it if you bought it for yourself' – if he bought it for someone else, it is not invalidated because it is a cancellation and a cancellation permits suspension. End. I say: If the pre-emptor before the sale says to the one who intends to buy: 'If you buy, then I have surrendered it,' is it valid or not? There is no doubt that it is a suspension of a cancellation before obligation due to the existence of its cause. And the implication of their statement that suspension by a pure condition is permissible in that which is from the category of pure cancellation, and their statement that the suspended thing is like an immediate act upon its existence, and their statement that one who does not have the power to execute immediately does not have the power to suspend unless he suspends it upon ownership or its cause – this shows the validity of the mentioned suspension because it is from the category of cancellation, as if he executed it immediately upon its existence and he suspended it upon ownership so reflect. But in al-Dhahiriyya there is something explicit that it is not a pure cancellation. Al-Dhahiriyya said in al-Fatawa al-Sughra: Suspension of the cancellation of pre-emption by a condition is permissible, even if he says 'I have surrendered to you the pre-emption of this house if you bought it for yourself,' then if he bought it for someone else, the pre-emptor remains on his pre-emption because surrender of pre-emption is a pure cancellation so its suspension by condition is valid. But there is an objection to this issue from what Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in the chapter of Conciliation on Crimes and the Book of Conciliation from al-Mabsut: that retaliation (qisas) – its suspension of cancellation by condition is not valid, nor does it permit addition to time, even though it is a pure cancellation. For this reason, it is not returned by the one who owes retaliation. And if he is coerced into surrendering pre-emption and he surrenders, his right to pre-emption is not invalidated. Thus it becomes clear that surrender of pre-emption is not a pure cancellation, because if it were a cancellation, it would be valid under coercion considering the general rule of cancellations. The issue is in Coercion of al-Mabsut. End. Suspension before the purchase is like immediate execution before it is not valid, and I have not seen anyone explicitly state the issue even though it occurs frequently, but what appears is the invalidity of suspension in it. And I ask Allah Almighty to find it in their words, for He is the Granter of success and the Helper. End.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage expands on the earlier point about including surrender of pre-emption (تسليم الشفعة) as a valid act for suspension. It begins by quoting al-Ramli from al-Bazaziyya that suspending the cancellation of pre-emption by a condition is permissible. The author (Ibn Nujaym) then considers a scenario where the pre-emptor says before the sale, 'If you buy, then I have surrendered it.' He argues that this is a suspension of a cancellation before the obligation arises, and since the rules of suspension for pure cancellations apply, it should be valid. However, he notes a contradiction from al-Dhahiriyya: while al-Dhahiriyya also says suspension of surrender of pre-emption is valid (because it is a pure cancellation), they cite al-Sarakhsi's view that retaliation (القصاص) cannot be suspended even though it is a pure cancellation, because coercion does not affect cancellations. From this, they deduce that surrender of pre-emption is not a pure cancellation because if it were, coercion would not invalidate it (but coercion does affect it). The passage ends with the author's own view that suspension before the purchase is invalid, but he has not found an explicit text to that effect and hopes to find it. This is a sophisticated intra-Hanafi debate about the nature of pre-emption cancellation.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of pre-emption; the right of a co-owner to purchase the share of a co-owner when sold to a third party.
إسقاط محض (isqāt maḥḍ): A pure cancellation that is not dependent on any consideration; e.g., divorce, manumission, and presumably surrender of pre-emption.
تسليم الشفعة (taslīm al-shuf'a): Surrender or waiver of the right of pre-emption.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'līq bi al-sharṭ): Suspension of a legal effect by a condition; the ruling becomes contingent upon the occurrence of a future event.

Key Takeaway
The nature of surrender of pre-emption as a pure cancellation is debated within the Hanafi school, with implications for its suspension and the effect of coercion.

Mortgage and Islam: Acts That Cannot Be Suspended
Critique of omissions on mortgage and Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish acts that cannot be suspended in Hanafi law and explain why mortgage is not an omission and why Islam cannot be conditional.

Core Idea
Mortgage survives corrupt conditions; Islam is an acknowledgment that cannot be suspended.

The commentator corrects the author's alleged omissions. Mortgage was already addressed in a previous context about corrupt conditions. The issue of Islam is subsumed under the rule that suspension of acknowledgment (iqrār) by condition is invalid. Understanding these principles prevents misapplication when dealing with conditional statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts criticized as omissions
Recognize that the passage mentions mortgage (rahn) and conversion to Islam (islam) as things the author supposedly missed.
Mortgage: a security contract; Islam: a declaration of faith.
2
Understand the defense for mortgage
The commentator notes that mortgage was already covered in the text under 'what is not invalidated by a corrupt condition', so it was not missed.
This precedent shows mortgage remains valid even if a corrupt condition is attached.
3
Analyze the ruling on conditional Islam
The text cites a fatwa: a dhimmi saying 'I am Muslim' conditionally does not become Muslim. The reason is that Islam is an acknowledgment (iqrār) of faith, and suspension of acknowledgment by condition is invalid.
Acknowledgment is a declaration of a pre-existing fact; conditions contradict its nature.
4
Derive the general principle
From these two examples, conclude that acts which are declaratory (like acknowledgment) cannot be suspended, while contractual acts (like mortgage) can survive corrupt conditions.
The distinction hinges on whether the act is a declaration or a contract.

قوله : (وقد فات المصنف (الرهن فيه أن الرهن مذكور في كلام المصنف فيما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد وتقدم مشروحاً. وقول وفاته أيضاً مسألة الإسلام سيأتي عن الغزي أنه داخل في الإقرار قوله : (كما في فتاوى قارئ الهداية قال الرملي نقلاً عن شيخ الإسلام محمد الغزي: الذي في فتاوى قارئ الهداية سئل إذا قال ذمي أنا مسلم أو إن فعلت كذا وأنا مسلم ثم فعله أو تلفظ بالشهادتين لا غير، هل يصير مسلماً؟ أجاب : لا يحكم بإسلامه في شيء من ذلك؛ كذا أفتى علماؤنا . ثم ذكر اختياره في ذلك فليراجع اهـ. وهو كما يخفى لا يفيد ما ذكره شيخنا فإن افتاءه الصحة ليس مبناها على التعليق وإنما هو مبني على أن قول الذمي أنا مسلم وأنا أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً رسول الله ليس بإسلام بل لا بد من التبري كما علمت تفاصيله في الكتب المبسوطة. وإنما يؤخذ عدم صحة تعليقه بالشرط من قولهم في المتون والشروح والفتاوى بعدم صحة تعليق الإقرار بالشرط وهذا ظاهر والله تعالى أعلم .اهـ. قوله : ويرد عليه أن الهبة الخ) أي يرد على الشارح الزيعلي وكأن الأولى تقديمه على قوله «وقد فات المصنف الخ» ولا يصح إرجاع الضمير للمصنف لما قد مر عن جامع الفصولين أن ما جاز تعليقه بالشرط لا تفسده الشروط الفاسدة، والمصنف عد هذه المذكورات مما لا تفسده الشروط الفاسدة، ولا ينافي ذلك جواز تعليقها. وقد مر أيضاً أن تعليق الوصية والإيصاء جائز، وكذا تعليق العزل عن القضاء، وكذا تعليق الحوالة والوكالة، فهذه قد فاتت الشارح أيضاً. وذكر في جامع الفصولين مما يجوز تعليقه إذن القن، وكذا تعليق النكاح والبراءة بشرط كائن حال، ولو قال بعته إن رضي فلان جاز البيع والشرط اهـ.. لكن إذا وقته بثلاثة أيام كم كما مر فراجعه.
His saying: (And the author missed mortgage) – in it, mortgage is mentioned in the author's speech in what is not invalidated by corrupt condition and it was previously explained. And his saying: he also missed the issue of Islam, it will come from al-Ghazzi that it is included in acknowledgement. His saying: (as in Fatawa Qari' al-Hidaya) – al-Ramli said, quoting from Shaykh al-Islam Muhammad al-Ghazzi: In the Fatawa of Qari' al-Hidaya, he was asked: If a dhimmi says 'I am Muslim' or 'If I do such-and-such then I am Muslim' and then he does it, or he utters the two testimonies only, does he become a Muslim? He answered: He is not judged to be Islam in any of that; thus our scholars gave fatwa. Then he mentioned his choice in that, so let it be reviewed. End. And it is, as is clear, not useful for what our teacher mentioned, because his fatwa of validity is not based on suspension, but rather on the fact that the dhimmi's saying 'I am Muslim' and 'I testify that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' is not Islam, but rather must include renunciation [of false religion] as you know its details in the detailed books. The invalidity of its suspension by condition is only taken from their statement in the texts, commentaries, and fatwas that suspension of acknowledgement by condition is not valid, and this is clear, and Allah knows best. End. His saying: (And it is objected to him regarding gift etc.) i.e., it is an objection to the commentator al-Zayla'i, and it seems preferable to present it before his saying 'And the author missed mortgage etc.' And it is not correct to refer the pronoun to the author because it has passed from Jami' al-Fusulayn that whatever is permitted to be suspended by condition is not corrupted by corrupt conditions, and the author counted these mentioned items as among those not corrupted by corrupt conditions, and that does not contradict the permissibility of their suspension. And it has also passed that suspension of will and bequest is permissible, and likewise suspension of removal from judgeship, and likewise suspension of hawala and agency – these have also been missed by the commentator. And it is mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn from what is permissible to suspend: permission of the slave, and likewise suspension of marriage and acquittal by a condition that exists, and if he said 'I sold it if so-and-so is pleased' – the sale and condition are valid. End. But if he limited it to three days, etc., as has passed, so review it.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the critique of the author's omissions. First, it addresses mortgage: the author already mentioned mortgage in the context of what is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so it was not missed. As for Islam, the commentator notes that some say it is included in acknowledgement (إقرار) and the suspension of acknowledgement by condition is invalid. The text refers to Fatawa Qari' al-Hidaya, where a dhimmi's statement 'I am Muslim' (even if conditional) is not considered Islam unless he explicitly renounces his prior religion; thus suspension of Islam is invalid. Then the commentator addresses the objection regarding gift: it would have been better to present that earlier. The commentator then lists other acts that can be suspended but were missed by the author and the commentator: suspension of will, bequest, removal from judgeship, hawala, agency, permission of a slave, marriage, and acquittal. These are from Jami' al-Fusulayn. The passage ends with a reminder to review the earlier discussion on time-limited conditions.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): Mortgage; a contract in which property is given as security for a debt.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Acknowledgment; here, a statement that one is Muslim, which is treated as an acknowledgment, and its suspension is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a dhimmi not considered Muslim simply by saying 'I am Muslim' (even conditionally)?
A) Because he did not utter the two testimonies
B) Because he must renounce his previous religion (tabarrī)
C) Because his statement is suspended
D) Because the condition was not fulfilled

Key Takeaway
Mortgage survives corrupt conditions, but suspension of an acknowledgment (like declaring Islam) by condition is invalid.

Acts That Can Be Suspended: Gift, Will, Agency, and Others
List of acts that can be suspended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the acts that Hanafi law permits to be suspended by a condition and explain the ruling that the condition is void but the underlying act remains valid.

Core Idea
Contracts like gift, will, and agency can be suspended; the condition falls away, but the act stands.

The passage continues by listing acts that can be suspended, correcting an earlier omission. These include gift, will, bequest, removal from judgeship, hawala, agency, permission of a slave, marriage, and acquittal. Understanding this list helps distinguish between acts that can be conditional and those that cannot.

Guided Path
1
Recall the principle from Jami' al-Fusulayn
The principle: 'Whatever is permitted to be suspended by condition is not corrupted by corrupt conditions.' This means if an act can be suspended, attaching a void condition does not invalidate the act itself.
This is a key maxim in Hanafi contracts.
2
Identify the acts listed as permissible to suspend
From the passage: gift, will, bequest, removal from judgeship, hawala, agency, permission of a slave, marriage, acquittal. Note that these are all contracts or unilateral dispositions.
The list is not exhaustive; the passage mentions these as examples.
3
Understand the corrective nature of the list
The commentator notes that these acts were missed by the earlier commentator (al-Zayla'i) and are now being corrected. This shows the importance of thoroughness in fiqh works.
The passage is a critique and expansion.
4
Apply the principle to a sample case
Take gift: if someone says 'I gift you this if you arrive', the gift is valid upon delivery, and the condition is ignored if it is corrupt (e.g., conditional on something prohibited).
The condition does not affect the validity of the gift itself.
5
Differentiate from acts that cannot be suspended
Compare with acknowledgment (lesson 1): those are declaratory and cannot be suspended, while these are contractual and can be.
The key is whether the act is a declaration of a pre-existing fact or a creation of a new obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Suspending Contracts on Conditions: The Hanafi Classification
Critique of al-Zayla'i on ta'liq contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify contracts into those that are invalidated by an invalid condition (shart fasid) and those that are not, and apply this classification to determine the validity of conditional contracts.

Core Idea
A corrupt condition voids contracts of mutual ownership transfer but not marriage or emancipation.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq critically examines earlier commentaries on a key fiqh issue: does an invalid condition always invalidate the contract? The author clarifies that the effect depends on the contract type. Some contracts, like sale and lease, are voided by any suspension; others, like marriage and khul', remain valid. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi law in contractual transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts mentioned as examples
List the contracts discussed in the passage: sale, lease, settlement for property, marriage, khul', emancipation for property, gift with compensation, surety, bequest, agency, etc.
Focus on the contracts explicitly said to be invalidated or not invalidated by a fasid condition.
2
Categorize into two groups
Group A: contracts invalidated by a fasid condition (sale, lease, settlement for property). Group B: contracts not invalidated (marriage, khul', emancipation for property). Also note contracts that can be validly suspended (gift with compensation, surety, etc.).
Contracts in Group A are those with mutual ownership transfer (tamlik wa tamalluk).
3
Understand the rationale
Contracts involving transfer of ownership require certainty in consideration and delivery; suspension creates uncertainty. Other contracts (marriage, khul') are more flexible and can tolerate conditions.
The rationale is rooted in the nature of each contract's purpose.
4
Recognize the author's critique
The author criticizes al-Zayla'i for omitting this classification, which could lead to erroneous fatwas if a mufti assumes all contracts are invalidated by fasid conditions.
The author supplements al-Zayla'i by citing al-Bazzaziyya and Jami' al-Fusulayn.
5
Apply to the dhimmi fatwa
The fatwa about a dhimmi's conditional declaration of faith is not about suspension but about the requirements of embracing Islam. The ruling is not based on ta'liq but on the need for explicit renunciation.
This distinction shows that not every conditional statement is a valid suspension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات
۳۲۰
كذا في جامع الفصولين وعلى هذا فما ذكره الكردري في المناقب معزياً إلى الناصحي لو قال إن اشتريت جارية فقد ملكتها منك يصح ومعناه إذا قبضه بناء على ذلك اهـ. مبني على أن الشرط ملائم. وفي البزازية من البيوع : وتعليق الهبة بـ (إن) باطل وبـ«على» إن ملائماً كهبته على أن يعوضه يجوز ، وإن مخالفاً بطل الشرط وصحت الهبة ويرد عليه أيضاً تعليق دعوة الولد صحيح كقوله إن كانت جاريتي حاملاً فمني صح ؛ كذا في البزازية وليس مما ذكره . وكذا يرد عليه الكفالة فإنه يصح تعليقها بشرط ملائم كما قدمناه ولم يذكر المصنف ولا الشارح ما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط الجائز وما لا يجوز وتقييده بالفاسد يخرجه، وفي البزازية: إن ما يتعلق بذكر الشرط الجائز يفسده الفاسد من الشرط كالبيع والإجارة والصلح على مال والقسمة وعقد لا يتعلق بالجائز. فالفاسد من الشرط لا يبطله كالنكاح والخلع والصلح عن العمد والعتق على مال فالأول لا يصح إلا ببدل منطوق معلوم يجري فيه التمليك والتملك، والثاني يصح ببدل وبدونه وببدل مجهول وحرام وحلال وعقد يتعلق بالجائز منه . والفاسد منه على نوعين : نوع يفسده ونوع لا وهو الكتابة إلى آخر ما فيها. وقد ذكر المصنف رحمه الله تعالى ما يجوز إضافته إلى زمان وما لا يجوز في آخر كتاب الإجارات فإذا وصلنا إليه شرحناه بأتم مما ذكره الشارح هنا وننبه على ما فاتهما إن شاء الله تعالى والله أعلم بالصواب.
دم [بعدم؟] في فتاوى قارئ الهداية سئل إذا قال ذمي أنا مسلم أو إن فعلت كذا وأنا مسلم ثم فعله أو تلفظ بالشهادتين لا غير، هل يصير مسلماً؟ أجاب : لا يحكم بإسلامه في شيء من ذلك؛ كذا أفتى علماؤنا . ثم ذكر اختياره في ذلك فليراجع اهـ. وهو كما يخفى لا يفيد ما ذكره شيخنا فإن افتاءه الصحة ليس مبناها على التعليق وإنما هو مبني على أن قول الذمي أنا مسلم وأنا أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً رسول الله ليس بإسلام بل لا بد من التبري كما علمت تفاصيله في الكتب المبسوطة. وإنما يؤخذ عدم صحة تعليقه بالشرط من قولهم في المتون والشروح والفتاوى بعدم صحة تعليق الإقرار بالشرط وهذا ظاهر والله تعالى أعلم .اهـ. قوله : ويرد عليه أن الهبة الخ) أي يرد على الشارح الزيعلي وكأن الأولى تقديمه على قوله «وقد فات المصنف الخ» ولا يصح إرجاع الضمير للمصنف لما قد مر عن جامع الفصولين أن ما جاز تعليقه بالشرط لا تفسده الشروط الفاسدة، والمصنف عد هذه المذكورات مما لا تفسده الشروط الفاسدة، ولا ينافي ذلك جواز تعليقها. وقد مر أيضاً أن تعليق الوصية والإيصاء جائز، وكذا تعليق العزل عن القضاء، وكذا تعليق الحوالة والوكالة، فهذه قد فاتت الشارح أيضاً. وذكر في جامع الفصولين مما يجوز تعليقه إذن القن، وكذا تعليق النكاح والبراءة بشرط كائن حال، ولو قال بعته إن رضي فلان جاز البيع والشرط اهـ.. لكن إذا وقته بثلاثة أيام كم كما مر فراجعه .
Likewise in Jami' al-Fusulayn: based on this, what al-Kardari mentioned in al-Manaqib, quoting al-Nasihi, that if one says 'If I buy a slave-girl, then I have owned her from you', it is valid, meaning when he takes possession based on that. It is based on the condition being compatible. In al-Bazzaziyya on sales: suspending a gift with 'if' is invalid, but with 'on condition' if compatible, like his gift on condition that he compensates him, is permissible; if incompatible, the condition is void and the gift is valid. Likewise, suspending the acknowledgment of a child is valid, like his saying 'If my slave-girl is pregnant, then the child is from me' is valid; as in al-Bazzaziyya, and it is not among what he mentioned. Similarly, surety is validly suspended with a compatible condition as we mentioned earlier. The author and the commentator did not mention what may be suspended with a valid condition and what may not; limiting it to the invalid condition excludes it. In al-Bazzaziyya: whatever is connected with mentioning a valid condition, the invalid condition corrupts it, like sale, lease, settlement for property, partition, and a contract that is not connected with the valid. The invalid condition does not invalidate it, like marriage, khul', settlement for intentional homicide, and emancipation for property. The first is not valid except with a stated known consideration involving transfer of ownership; the second is valid with or without consideration, and with unknown, forbidden, or lawful consideration, and a contract connected with the valid part of it. The invalid part is of two types: one type invalidates it and one does not, which is kitabah... up to the end of what is in it. The author has mentioned what may be added to time and what may not in the last part of the Book of Leases; when we reach it we will explain it more fully than what the commentator mentioned here, and we will point out what they both missed, God willing. God knows best what is correct.
A [question?] in Fatawa Qari' al-Hidaya: he was asked if a dhimmi says 'I am Muslim' or 'If I do such-and-such and I am Muslim' then does it, or utters the two testimonies only, does he become a Muslim? He answered: he is not judged to be Muslim in any of that; such was the fatwa of our scholars. Then he mentioned his choice in this, so let it be consulted. It is, as is clear, not useful for what our shaykh mentioned, because his fatwa of validity is not based on suspension but rather on the fact that the dhimmi's saying 'I am Muslim and I testify that there is no god but Allah and Muhammad is His Messenger' is not Islam; rather, he must also renounce [the religion of the dhimmi] as you have learned its details in the expanded books. The invalidity of suspending it on a condition is taken from their statement in the texts, commentaries, and fatwas of the invalidity of suspending an acknowledgment on a condition, and this is apparent. God knows best.
His saying: 'Also, it may be objected that the gift...' meaning it is an objection to the commentator al-Zayla'i, and it would have been better to place it before his saying 'And the author omitted...' and it is not correct to refer the pronoun to the author, as has already been mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn that what is validly suspended by a condition is not corrupted by invalid conditions, and the author counted these mentioned items among those that are not corrupted by invalid conditions, and that does not contradict the permissibility of suspending them. It has also been mentioned that suspending a bequest and a directive is valid, likewise suspending dismissal from judgeship, likewise suspending hawala and agency; these the commentator also missed. It is mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn among what may be suspended: the permission of a slave, likewise suspending marriage and acquittal on a condition present at the time, and if he says 'I sold it if so-and-so is pleased', the sale and the condition are valid; but if he specifies three days, etc., as previously, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the commentary by al-Zayla'i on the Hidayah. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq points out that al-Zayla'i and the original author (al-Marghinani) omitted discussing which contracts can be validly suspended on a condition. The author clarifies that there are contracts that are validly suspended with a compatible condition (such as gift with compensation, surety, acknowledgment of lineage), and contracts that are invalidated by any condition (like sale, lease). However, some contracts like marriage and khul' are not invalidated by a corrupt condition. The author then critiques a fatwa by Qari' al-Hidaya about a dhimmi's conditional declaration of faith, arguing that the fatwa's ruling is not based on suspension but on the requirement of explicit renunciation. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between contracts that can tolerate conditional suspension and those that cannot, with practical examples from the madhhab's authoritative texts.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a contract's effect on a future condition (shart).
شرط جائز (shart ja'iz): A condition that is permissible and compatible with the contract's nature.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is invalid because it contradicts the contract's purpose or is against Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of contract remains valid even if a fasid (invalid) condition is attached?
A) Sale
B) Marriage
C) Lease
D) Settlement for property

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the effect of an invalid condition depends on the contract type: it voids contracts of ownership transfer but does not void marriage and similar flexible contracts.

Introduction to Sarf: Definition and Conditions
Defines sarf linguistically and legally, and begins listing its four conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sarf and list its four conditions for validity.

Core Idea
Sarf is a currency exchange contract requiring immediate hand-to-hand delivery and, if same genus, equality in weight to prevent riba.

This lesson introduces the Book of Sarf from al-Bahr al-Raiq. Sarf governs the exchange of monetary items like gold and silver. We will learn its linguistic and legal meanings, pillars, and the four specific conditions that make it valid.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic and legal meanings
Note the root meaning of 'sarf' as excess/exchange in language, and how it translates to currency exchange in Shari'ah.
Linguistic meaning helps understand the term's scope.
2
Identify the legal definition
Sarf is defined as 'the sale of some valuables (thaman) for others.' Understand that thaman includes not only gold/silver bullion but also manufactured items made from them.
The definition covers both pure and manufactured monetary items.
3
Recognize the pillars
The pillars of sarf are the same as any sale: offer (ijab), acceptance (qabul), or mutual exchange (ta'ati).
No special pillars beyond the general sale contract.
4
Memorize the four conditions
The four conditions for validity are: (1) hand-to-hand possession before separation (taqabudh), (2) contract must be definitive (batt) with no option (khiyar al-shart), (3) no deferment of either countervalue, (4) equality in weight if same genus.
These conditions prevent riba.
5
Note exceptions for khiyar
Option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) is allowed; option of sight (khiyar al-ru'ya) only for specific items (ayn) not debts.
Khiyar al-shart is only allowed if annulled before separation.

Source Text

Book of Currency Exchange: It is the sale of some of the valuables for others. If they are of the same genus, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are conditions; if they differ in quality... The reason for its delay has preceded. Discussion is in several places: First, its linguistic meaning. It is mentioned in al-Qamus that 'sarf' of speech is to increase in it and embellish it, derived from sarf in dirhams, which is the excess of some over others in value. Likewise, sarf of speech. As for sarf in the hadith 'Allah does not accept from him any sarf or 'adl', sarf is repentance and 'adl is ransom; or it is supererogatory and 'adl is obligatory; or the opposite; or it is weight and 'adl is measure; or it is acquisition and 'adl is ransom or tricks. In al-Sihah: it is said, I exchanged dirhams for dinars, and between the two dirhams there is sarf, meaning the superiority of the silver quality of one over the other. Second, its meaning in Shari'ah, which he has indicated by his saying: 'It is the sale of some valuables for others,' like gold and silver when one is sold for the other, i.e., the sale of some of the genus of valuables for others. We interpreted it like this and did not leave it on its apparent meaning to include the sale of manufactured items for manufactured items or for cash, because manufactured items due to the workmanship attached to them are no longer explicit currency, therefore in the contract it is specified as a sarf sale. Third, its pillar: whatever is the pillar of every sale is its pillar, consisting of offer and acceptance or mutual exchange (ta'ati). Fourth, its conditions: they are four: 1) Taking possession of both countervalues before separation from the place (qabd before iftiraq). 2) It must be definitive (batt) with no option (khiyar). If an option is stipulated and the owner annuls it before separation, it is valid; after separation it is not. As for option of defect, it is established in sarf. As for option of sight, it is established for a specific (ayn) item but not for a debt. If he returns it due to a defect, the contract is rescinded, whether he returns it in the session or afterward. If it was a debt and he returns it in the session, the contract is not rescinded; if he returns its substitute, the sarf remains; if he returns it after separation, it becomes void. The complete discussion is in al-Bada'i'. 3) The countervalue of sarf must not be deferred (mu'ajjal). If the party with the deferred term annuls the deferment before separation and pays what is due, then they separate after possession from both sides, it becomes valid; after separation, it does not. 4) Equality in weight if the object of contract is of the same genus. If they exchange gold... (text breaks off). Al-Bahr al-Raiq vol. 6 p. 21
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Sarf (currency exchange) from al-Bahr al-Raiq. It first explains the linguistic meaning of 'sarf' as excess or exchange, quoting classical lexicons. Then it gives the legal definition: the sale of one type of currency (thaman) for another. The author clarifies that this includes manufactured gold and silver items because they are no longer pure currency but still fall under sarf. The pillars of sarf are the same as any sale (offer and acceptance or mutual exchange). The conditions specific to sarf are four: (1) hand-to-hand delivery before the parties separate, (2) no option (khiyar) except the option of defect which remains, (3) no deferment of either countervalue, and (4) equality in weight if the two items are of the same genus. The text also discusses special rules for option of sight and defect. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi rulings on transactions involving monetary exchange, emphasizing riba prevention.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): The sale of one type of currency (thaman) for another, e.g., gold for silver.
ثمن (thaman): Price or currency; that which is used as a medium of exchange.
تقابض (taqabudh): Mutual hand-to-hand delivery of both countervalues before the parties separate.
تماثل (tamathul): Equality in weight when exchanging the same genus (e.g., gold for gold).
خيار (khiyar): Option to cancel the contract; khiyar al-shart (condition option) is not allowed in sarf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No deferment of payment
C) Equality in weight
D) Contract is definitive (no khiyar al-shart)

Key Takeaway
Sarf is a currency exchange contract requiring immediate hand-to-hand delivery and, if same genus, equality in weight to prevent riba.

Post-Contract Increase or Decrease in Currency Exchange: Three Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on post-contract increase/reduction in sarf with usul basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on a post-contract increase or reduction in a same-genus currency exchange, and explain the usul principle (attachment of a later corrupt condition) that underlies the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A corrupt condition mentioned after contract may or may not attach—determining whether a later increase/reduction invalidates the original sale.

You have learned that a valid currency exchange (sarf) requires equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery before separation. But what happens if, after the exchange is complete and the parties have parted, one later gives an extra coin or reduces the amount? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals a classic intra-Hanafi dispute, where Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each give a different ruling. The difference traces back to a fundamental usul question: does a corrupt condition (shart fasid) mentioned after the contract but intended to be part of it actually attach to the contract? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how usul principles produce distinct fiqh rulings even within one madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base case
Start with a completed same-genus currency exchange: two people exchange gold for gold, hand-to-hand, and then separate (tafarruq). Later, one party gives an increase (ziyada) or reduction (hut) in the amount, and the other accepts. What is the effect on the original sale?
The conditions of tamathul and taqabud were met at the time of contract.
2
State the three positions
Recall the three positions: Abu Hanifa says the sale becomes fasid (invalid) for both increase and reduction. Abu Yusuf says both increase and reduction are invalid but the original sale remains sahih (valid). Muhammad distinguishes: increase invalidates the sale, reduction is valid as an independent gift.
Memorize each position and its underlying rationale.
3
Trace the usul principle
The ikhtilaf originates from a dispute on whether a later corrupt condition (shart fasid muta'akhir) attaches to the original contract when mentioned after the contract but intended to be part of it. Abu Hanifa holds it attaches and vitiates the contract; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it does not attach, except Muhammad considers increase as a corrupt condition that does attach due to its riba-like nature.
Understand that this is not just a fiqh rule but a usul divergence within the school.
4
Note the exception for different-genus exchange
If the exchange involves different genera (e.g., gold for silver), a post-contract increase or reduction is valid by consensus, provided the increase is taken before separation to maintain the condition of hand-to-hand delivery.
This shows the principle is context-sensitive.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, a buyer who later gives extra gold must redo the exchange contract. Under Abu Yusuf, the original transaction stands and the extra is considered a void gift. Under Muhammad, reduction is a valid gift, but increase requires a new contract for the excess.
This affects how a mufti advises in real transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو تجانسا شرط التماثل والتقابض) أي النقدان بأن أحدهما ومن قبض البدلين قبل الافتراق. أما التساوي فقدمناه في التساوي وزناً. من لصحته بد عدم فرع باب الربا ولو تصارفا جنساً بجنس مثلاً بمثل وتقابضا وتفرقا ثم زاد أحدهما صاحبه شيئاً أو حط عنه شيئاً وقبله الآخر فسد البيع عند أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف هما باطلان والصرف صحيح، وعند محمد الزيادة باطلة والحط جائز بمنزلة الهبة المستقلة. واختلافهم هذا اختلافهم في أن الشرط الفاسد المتأخر عن العقد في الذكر إذا ألحق به هل يلتحق أم لا؛ فمن أصل أبي حنيفة التحاقه ويفسد العقد ومن أصلهما التحاقه فطرده أبو يوسف هنا، ومحمد فرق بين الزيادة والحط ولو زاد أو حط في صرف بخلاف الجنس جاز إجماعاً لكن يشترط قبض الزيادة قبل الافتراق لالتحاقها بأصل العقد. ولو حط مشتري الدينار قيراطاً منها فبائع الدينار يكون شريكاً له في الدينار. ولو زاد مشتري السيف المحلى ديناراً جاز، ولا يشترط قبضه قبل الافتراق لصرف الزيادة إلى النصل والحمل وتمامه في البدائع.
His saying (If they are of the same genus, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are conditions) meaning the two types of currency: that one of them and acceptance of the two countervalues before separation. As for equality, we have presented it regarding equality by weight. For its validity, it depends on the absence of [defect]. Branch on usury: If two people exchange a genus for a genus like for like, take possession, separate, then one gives an increase or reduction to the other and the other accepts, the sale is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, both are invalid but the exchange itself is valid. According to Muhammad, the increase is invalid but the reduction is valid as an independent gift. Their difference is their difference regarding whether a corrupt condition mentioned after the contract but attached to it is considered attached or not. According to Abu Hanifa's principle, it is attached and nullifies the contract. According to their principle, it is attached. Abu Yusuf applied this consistently here, while Muhammad distinguished between increase and reduction. If one increases or reduces in an exchange of different types, it is valid by consensus, but it is a condition that the increase be taken before separation because it attaches to the original contract. If the buyer of a dinar reduces a carat from it, then the seller of the dinar becomes a partner in the dinar. If the buyer of a gilded sword adds a dinar, it is valid, and its taking before separation is not a condition because the increase goes to the blade and the scabbard. Its completion is in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a branch (far') in the chapter on riba regarding currency exchange (sarf). It opens by reiterating the conditions for exchanging same-genus currencies: equality in weight (tamathul) and hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) before separation (tafarruq). It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens if, after a valid exchange contract has been concluded and the parties have separated, one of them later gives an increase or reduction (hut) in price. The core issue is whether such a later corrupt condition attaches back to the original contract. Imam Abu Hanifa: both increase and reduction render the original sale invalid (fasid) because the later condition is considered attached and the contract was based on something corrupt. Imam Abu Yusuf: both the increase and reduction are invalid actions, but the original exchange remains valid (sahih) since the later condition does not attach. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguishes: increase invalidates the sale (since it resembles a forbidden surplus), but reduction is valid as an independent gift (hiba), leaving the original exchange intact. The text explains this difference stems from a usul principle: whether a later corrupt condition attaches to the contract. Abu Hanifa holds it attaches; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it does not, but Muhammad makes an exception for increase as it involves riba. The passage also notes that for exchange of different types (e.g., gold for silver), both increase and reduction are valid by consensus, but the increase must be taken before separation unless it is incidental (like the sword's embellishment).

Key Terms
التماثل (al-tamathul): Equality in weight for same-genus ribawi items in an exchange contract.
التقابض (al-taqabud): Physical hand-to-hand delivery of both countervalues before the parties separate.
الشرط الفاسد المتأخر (al-shart al-fasid al-muta'akhir): A condition that is legally corrupt and is mentioned after the contract but intended to be part of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what is the legal status of a post-contract increase in a same-genus currency exchange?
A) The increase is valid and the original sale is valid.
B) The increase is invalid and the original sale is invalid.
C) The increase is invalid but the original sale remains valid.
D) The increase is valid and the original sale becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
A later increase or reduction in a same-genus exchange triggers a three-way intra-Hanafi dispute rooted in whether a corrupt condition attaches to the contract; the difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
