Gift, Substitution, and Offset in Sarf
Explains the effect of gifting, substituting, and offsetting in sarf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on gifting, substituting, and offsetting the price in a sarf contract, and identify when the contract becomes annulled or remains valid.

Core Idea
In sarf, actions that bypass immediate possession invalidate the contract.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq examines several scenarios that affect a sarf (currency exchange) contract. The author explains how actions like gifting the exchanged currency, substituting it before possession, or offsetting it against a later debt can annul the contract or leave it intact. Understanding these rulings is essential for knowing the boundaries of valid exchange in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core actions
The passage addresses three actions: gifting the price, substituting it before possession, and offsetting it against a later debt. Each has a specific ruling based on possession and consent.
These actions are treated as potential cancellations (faskh) of the sarf contract.
2
Analyze the role of possession (qabd)
In sarf, immediate hand-to-hand possession is a condition for validity. Any action that bypasses this requirement—like substitution or offsetting before qabd—is prohibited or invalid.
The requirement of qabd is derived from the hadith on exchanging gold for silver.
3
Determine annulment vs. validity
For a gift: if accepted, the contract is annulled; if not, the gift is invalid and the contract remains. For substitution: not allowed before possession. For offsetting: not allowed even with mutual consent. For third-party claim: depends on whether the claimant validates or reclaims.
The key is whether the action effectively circumvents the condition of qabd.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Work through the example of a currency exchange where one party attempts to gift or offset the currency. Determine whether the contract is valid or annulled based on the rules above.
Practice with the scenarios in the passage to solidify understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هبته والتصدق به فإن فعل لم يصح بدون قبول الآخر، فإن قبل انتقض الصرف وإلا لم يصح ولم ينتقض لأنه في معنى الفسخ فلا يصح إلا بتراضيهما، فلو أبي الواهب أن يأخذ ما وهب أجبر على القبض، وتفرع أيضاً أنه لا يجوز الاستبدال ببدل الصرف قبل قبضه وسيأتي . وعلى هذا تتخرج المقاصة في ثمن الصرف إذا وجب الدين بعقد متأخر عن عقد الصرف أنه قصاصاً ببدل الصرف وإن تراضيا بذلك وقد مر في السلم. ولو قبض بدل الصرف ثم انتقض القبض فيه لمعنى أوجب انتقاضه أن يبطل الصرف وقد تقدم في السلم وتمامه في البدائع. ثم إن استحق أحد بدلي الصرف بعد الافتراق فإن أجاز المستحق والبدل قائم أو ضمن الناقد وهو هالك جاز الصرف، وإن استرده وهو قائم أو ضمن القابض قيمته وهو هالك بطل الصرف ؛ كذا في البدائع. قيدنا التماثل من حيث الوزن لأنه لا اعتبار به عدداً؛ كذا يصير في الذخيرة.
His gift and charity - if he does so, it is not valid without the acceptance of the other. If he accepts, the sarf is annulled; otherwise it is not valid and not annulled because it is in the meaning of rescission, so it is not valid except with mutual consent. If the donor refuses to take what he has given, he is compelled to take possession. It is also derived that substitution for the price of sarf before its possession is not allowed, and it will come. Based on this, offsetting in the price of sarf is derived if the debt becomes due by a later contract after the sarf contract, that it is an offset by the price of sarf even if they mutually agree, and it has passed in al-Salam. If the price of sarf was received and then the receipt is annulled due to a reason that necessitates its annulment, then the sarf is invalid, and it has preceded in al-Salam and its completion is in al-Bada'i. Then if one of the two items of sarf is claimed after separation, if the claimant validates it and the item exists, or the payer guarantees it while it is destroyed, the sarf is valid. If he reclaims it while it exists, or the receiver guarantees its value while it is destroyed, the sarf is invalid. This is in al-Bada'i. We restricted similitude in terms of weight because it is not considered by count; thus it is in al-Dhakhira.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on various scenarios in a sarf (currency exchange) contract. The author addresses the consequences of gifting or giving in charity the exchanged item before full possession. Such actions are treated as a cancellation (faskh) and require mutual acceptance. If the counterparty accepts the gift, the sarf contract is annulled; otherwise it remains but the gift is invalid. The donor is compelled to take possession if he refuses. The passage then extends to the ruling on substituting the price before possession—it is prohibited. Offsetting (muqasah) in the price of sarf is not valid even if the parties agree, because it effectively circumvents the requirement of hand-to-hand delivery. If possession is validly taken and then later annulled due to a reason (like the item being defective), the sarf contract is void. The passage also discusses the scenario where a third party claims ownership of one of the exchanged items after the parties have separated. If the rightful owner validates the transaction while the item is still in hand or if the exchanger pays its value (in case it is destroyed), the sarf remains valid. But if the owner reclaims the item while it exists, or if the receiver pays its value (it being destroyed), the sarf becomes invalid. The author notes that the requirement of similitude is by weight, not count, for gold and silver.

Key Terms
بدل الصرف (badal al-sarf): The price or countervalue in a currency exchange contract.
مقاصة (muqāṣṣah): Offsetting a debt with a reciprocal debt; here, setting off the price of sarf against a later debt.
انتقض القبض (intaqaḍa al-qabḍ): The annulment or invalidation of possession after it was validly taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone sells a dinar for dirhams (sarf) and then gifts the dirhams to the buyer before the buyer accepts, what is the ruling?
A) The gift is valid and the sarf is annulled.
B) The gift is invalid and the sarf remains.
C) The gift is invalid and the sarf is annulled.
D) The gift is valid and the sarf remains.

Key Takeaway
In a sarf contract, any action (gift, substitution, offset) that circumvents immediate hand-to-hand possession invalidates the contract unless properly executed with mutual consent and actual delivery.

Exchange of Gold and Silver with Difference in Quality or Workmanship
Cites hadith to justify permissibility of exchanging gold and silver of different quality or workmanship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging gold and silver that differ in quality or workmanship, identify the hadith evidence, and apply the ruling to distinguish between ribawi items.

Core Idea
Difference in quality does not permit riba when types are same; only different types allow free exchange hand to hand.

When two parties wish to exchange gold for gold or silver for silver, the hadith demands equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery. But what if one piece is of higher quality or crafted into jewelry? This lesson clarifies that such differences are irrelevant for riba purposes; only weight and immediate exchange matter when the type is the same. The Hanafi school relies on the generality of the prophetic hadith to permit exchange when types differ, regardless of quality or craftsmanship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is exchanging gold or silver that differ in quality or workmanship. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) under the conditions derived from the hadith.
Focus on the type of items: same type (gold/gold) vs different types (gold/silver).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith narrated by Muslim: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver... if the types differ, sell as you wish if hand to hand.' This hadith establishes the rules for ribawi items.
The hadith is ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'if the types differ' (فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف) indicates that when the genus changes (gold for silver), equality in weight is not required; only hand-to-hand delivery is necessary. When the type is the same, equality in weight is required regardless of quality or workmanship.
Quality (joudah) and workmanship (siyaghah) are not considered differences in type.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement regarding selling two identical items of the same type and quality. Muhammad al-Shaybani and some early scholars considered it impermissible, but the relied-upon position permits it.
This ikhtilaf is recorded in al-Dhakhira.
5
Apply the distinction based on custom
For other ribawi items like copper, the ruling depends on custom: if customarily sold by weight, riba rules apply; if by count, they are not ribawi. This distinction is relevant for modern commodities.
Gold and silver retain their riba characteristics regardless of custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن اختلفا جودة وصياغة) لقوله عليه السلام الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة» إلى أن قال مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء، يداً بيد فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يداً بيد» (۱) رواه مسلم وغيره. ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكونا مما يتعين بالتعيين كالمصوغ والتبرأ ولا يتعينان كالمضروب، أو يتعين أحدهما دون الآخر لإطلاق الحديث، وفي الذخيرة من البيوع من الفصل السادس : وإذا باع درهماً كبيراً بدرهم صغيراً أو درهماً جيداً بدرهم رديء يجوز لأن لهما فيه غرضاً صحيحاً، فأما إذا كانا مستويين في القدر والصفة فبيع أحدهما بالآخر هل يجوز وهل يصير مثله ديناً في الذمة؟ اختلفوا بعضهم قالوا: لا يجوز وأشار إليه محمد في الكتاب وبه كان يفتي أبو حاتم الإمام أبو أحمد اهـ. قيد إسقاط الصفة بالأثمان لأنه لو باع إناء نحاساً بإناء نحاس أحدهما أثقل من الآخر فإنه يجوز وزناً . النحاس وغيره مما يوزن من الأموال الربوية أيضاً، وذلك لأن صفة الوزن في النقدين عليها فلا يتغير بالصنعة ولا يخرج عن كونه موزوناً بتعارف جعله عددياً لو تعورف ذلك بخلاف غيرهما فإن الوزن فيه بالتعارف فيخرج عن كونه موزوناً بتعارف عدديته إذا صيغ وصنع ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الذخيرة حتى قالوا: لو اعتادوا الأواني المتخذة بيع من هذه الأشياء بالوزن لا بالعدد لا يجوز بيعه بغير المصنوع من جنسه إلا متساوياً وزناً، وإذا تعاملوا بيعها عدداً لا وزناً يجوز بيع الواحد بالإثنين .اهـ. وفي القاموس : الجيد ككيس ضد الرديء والجمع جياد وجيادات وجيايد، وجاد يجود جودة صار جيداً اهـ. وفيه : والصياغة بالكسر حرفة الصائغ اهـ
His statement: (And if they differ in quality and workmanship) due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver' until he said: 'like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand. If these types differ, then sell as you wish if it is hand to hand.' (Narrated by Muslim and others). And there is no difference in that between items that are specified by designation like jewelry and bullion, and those not specified like coins, or one specified without the other, due to the generality of the hadith. And in al-Dhakhira, from the book of sales, chapter six: If someone sells a large dirham for a small dirham, or a good dirham for a bad dirham, it is permissible because they have a valid purpose. But if they are equal in size and quality, is selling one for the other permissible and does it become a debt in the obligation? Some differed: some said it is not permissible, and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) indicated it in the book, and Abu Hatim al-Imam Abu Ahmad used to give fatwa accordingly. The dropping of the description is restricted to the two currencies because if someone sells a copper vessel for a copper vessel, one heavier than the other, it is permissible by weight. Copper and other weighable items from ribawi properties also, because the attribute of weight in the two currencies is inherent and does not change by craftsmanship, nor does it exit from being weighable by customary counting if so customary, unlike other items where weight is by custom and they exit from being weighable by customary counting when forged and crafted; thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Dhakhira, even they said: If people customarily sell vessels by weight, not by count, selling them for something other than its own kind is not permissible except equal by weight. If they trade them by count, not weight, selling one for two is permissible. In al-Qamus: al-jayyid (good) like kays, opposite of bad; plural jiād, jiyādāt, jayāyid. Jād yajūd jūdah: became good. And therein: al-ṣiyāghah (craftsmanship) with kasrah: the profession of the jeweler.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) addressing the exchange of gold and silver that differ in quality (jouda) or workmanship (siyagha). The author cites the well-known hadith from Sahih Muslim: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand; if the types differ, sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' This hadith clearly indicates that when the two currencies are of the same type (gold for gold, silver for silver), equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery are required. But if the types differ (gold for silver), only hand-to-hand delivery is required, and equality in weight or quality is not necessary. The passage then notes that this ruling applies regardless of whether the items are designated as specific 'ayn (like jewelry or bullion) or not (like coins), due to the generality of the hadith. The text from al-Dhakhira elaborates: selling a large dirham for a small dirham, or a good one for a bad one, is permissible because both parties have a valid purpose. However, if they are equal in weight and quality, there is a disagreement: some scholars, including Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that it is not permissible (because it is a form of riba al-fadl?), while others allow it. The author then clarifies that the attribute of quality is disregarded only for gold and silver, because weight is inherent in them and does not change by craftsmanship. For other weighable items like copper, their categorization as weighable or countable depends on custom; if they are customarily sold by weight, then riba rules apply; if by count, they are not ribawi. The author also provides linguistic definitions of jayyid and siyaghah.

Key Terms
جودة (jūdah): Quality, used here to mean good or superior grade of gold/silver.
صياغة (ṣiyāghah): Workmanship; the craft of a jeweler, here meaning whether the metal is crafted (jewelry) or not (bullion).
تعين بالتعيين (ta'ayyun bi al-ta'yīn): Becoming specified by designation; meaning an item that is identified as a specific object (e.g., a particular necklace) rather than a generic weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, when selling gold for silver with different quality, what is required?
A) Equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery.
B) Hand-to-hand delivery and equality in quality.
C) Only hand-to-hand delivery, not equality in weight or quality.
D) Equality in weight but not hand-to-hand delivery.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits exchanging gold and silver of differing quality or workmanship as long as the exchange is hand-to-hand, because the hadith only requires equality when the types are the same.

Condition of Qabd in Sarf When Types Differ
Explains the condition of qabd in sarf with different types and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qabd in sarf when types differ, distinguish between qabd as a condition for formation (in'iqaad) vs. remaining validity (baqa'), and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a scenario involving a defect.

Core Idea
In sarf with different types, only hand-to-hand delivery is required; it is a condition for the contract's continuing validity, not its formation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the condition of qabd (hand-to-hand delivery) when the two items in a sarf exchange are of different types, such as gold for silver. It establishes that only mutual possession before separation is required, not equality in weight. Furthermore, it resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether qabd is a condition for the contract's initial validity or its remaining validity, and explains the practical consequence of this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Determine what is required for a sarf contract when the two items are of different types (e.g., gold vs. silver). The rule is that only mutual hand-to-hand delivery (qabd) before separation is needed, not equality in weight.
This contrasts with the rule for same-type exchanges where both equality and qabd are required.
2
Define qabd as used here
Understand the technical meaning of qabd in this context: actual physical hand-to-hand transfer (bi al-barājim), not mere relinquishment (takhliyah). This is based on Fawa'id al-Quduri.
In other contracts, takhliyah may suffice, but not in sarf.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the statement reported in the hadith: 'If they separate before qabd, it becomes void.' This is a dalīl naqlī.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim but is referenced as the basis.
4
Trace the ikhtilaf about qabd's nature
Some Hanafi scholars say qabd is a condition for the contract's valid formation (shart in'iqaad). Others, including the correct opinion, say it is a condition for the contract's remaining validity (shart baqa'). Analyze the proof for the second view: separation voids the contract only if it was initially valid.
The objection that qabd is physically subsequent is answered by treating it as legally concurrent.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a defect (fasad) appears in the sarf part of a transaction, does it spread to a non-sarf part? On the weak opinion (qabd as shart in'iqaad), it does; on the correct opinion (shart baqa'), it does not.
This shows the importance of the distinction in multi-item transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإلا شرط التقابض) أي وإن لم يتجانسا يشترط التقابض قبل الافتراق دون التماثل لما رويناه من الحديث. وفي فتح القدير والمعراج معزياً إلى فوائد القدوري : المراد بالقبض هنا القبض بالبراجم لا بالتخلية يريد باليد اهـ. ثم اختلفوا في القبض فقيل شرط انعقاده صحيحاً فأورد عليه أنه حينئذ لا بد من القرآن أو التقدم والقبض متأخر فكان حكماً له لا شرطاً وأجيب بأن الوجود في المجلس جعل مقارناً للعقد حكماً، والصحيح المختار أنه شرط بقائه على الصحة لا شرط انعقاده وقد أشار محمد إلى كل منهما كما في الذخيرة. ويدل على الثاني قوله فإن تفرقا قبل القبض بطل فلولا أنه منعقد لما بطل بالافتراق ؛ كذا في المعراج وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا ظهر الفساد فيما هو صرف فهل يفسد فيما ليس بصرف عند أبي حنيفة فعلى القول الضغيف يتعدى الفساد وعلى الأصح لا يتعدى؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وقيد بالذهب والفضة لأنه لو باع فضة بفلوس أو ذهب بفلوس فإنه يشترط قبض أحد البدلين قبل الافتراق لا قبضهما ؛ كذا في الذخيرة وقدمناه عند قوله في باب الربا وصح بيع الفلس بالفلسين
His statement: (And otherwise, the condition of mutual hand-to-hand delivery) meaning if they are not homogeneous, mutual hand-to-hand delivery before separation is required, not equality, due to the hadith we narrated. And in Fath al-Qadir and al-Mi'raj, attributing to Fawa'id al-Quduri: the intended meaning of qabd here is hand-to-hand (bi al-barājim) not by relinquishment (takhliyah), meaning with the hand. Then they differed regarding qabd: some said it is a condition for the contract's valid formation. An objection was raised: in that case, the contract would necessarily require a preceding [offer] and the qabd is subsequent, so it would be a consequence not a condition. The answer was that existence in the session is considered concurrent with the contract by legal ruling. The correct and chosen opinion is that it is a condition for its remaining validity, not for its formation, and Muhammad indicated both. And evidence for the second is his statement: 'If they separate before qabd, it becomes void' — for unless it was validly formed, separation would not void it. Thus in al-Mi'raj. The practical consequence of the dispute appears if a defect appears in what is sarf: does it also invalidate a non-sarf part? According to Abu Hanifa, on the weak opinion the invalidity extends; on the correct opinion it does not. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is restricted to gold and silver because if someone sells silver for fulus (copper coins) or gold for fulus, only one of the two items must be received before separation, not both; thus in al-Dhakhira, and we have presented it at his statement in the chapter of riba: 'And the sale of a fals for two fals is valid.'
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that clarifies the condition of qabd (hand-to-hand delivery) when the two currencies are of different types (e.g., gold for silver). The author explains that only qabd before separation is required, not equality in weight. The qabd here is defined as physical hand-to-hand transfer (بالبراجم), not mere relinquishment (تخلية). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether qabd is a condition for the contract's initial validity (shart in'iqaad) or for its remaining validity (shart baqa'). The correct and chosen opinion is that it is a condition for the remaining validity, because if the contract were not initially valid, separation would not void it. The practical consequence (thamara) appears if a defect (fasad) arises in a sarf contract: does it also affect a non-sarf contract included in the same transaction? According to Abu Hanifa, on the weak opinion the fasad spreads, but on the correct view it does not. The passage also notes that this restriction applies only to gold and silver; for items like fulus (copper coins), only one of the two items needs to be received before separation, not both, because fulus are not considered pure ribawi property in the same way.

Key Terms
إلا شرط التقابض (illā sharṭ al-taqābuḍ): Unless the condition of mutual hand-to-hand delivery is fulfilled; i.e., when types differ, only qabd is required.
القبض بالبراجم (al-qabḍ bi al-barājim): Physical hand-to-hand transfer using the fingers; actual manual possession.
شرط بقاء (sharṭ baqā’): A condition for the contract's continuing validity, not its initial formation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A condition for the contract's valid formation (shart in'iqaad).
B) A condition for the contract's remaining validity (shart baqa').
C) A recommended practice (sunnah) that does not affect validity.
D) An obligatory element (wajib) whose omission requires compensation.

Key Takeaway
In sarf with different currency types, hand-to-hand delivery before separation is a condition for the contract's remaining validity, not its formation.

Selling Gold for Silver by Guess (Mujazafah) – Conditions and Validity
Ruling on guess sale in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid gold-silver sale by guess and identify when the sale becomes invalid.

Core Idea
Guess sale of different types is valid if hand-to-hand delivery occurs before separation.

In sarf (currency exchange), many assume that weight must always be known. However, when exchanging different types like gold for silver, the Prophet's hadith only requires hand-to-hand delivery (qabd) in the session. Guess (mujazafah) does not invalidate the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exchanged items
Gold and silver are different genera (jins) in ribawi items. Recognize that the sale is of one type for another, not the same type.
This triggers a different ruling than same-genre exchange.
2
Recognize the method of sale: guess (mujazafah)
The sale is made without exact weight or measurement. This is permissible when types differ.
If types were the same, guess would invalidate unless equality is known.
3
Apply the key condition: hand-to-hand delivery in the session
The only required condition is qabd (physical exchange) before the parties separate. Equality in weight is not needed.
The hadith 'yadan bi yadin' (hand-to-hand) is the basis.
4
Determine when the sale becomes void
If the parties separate before both items are received, or before one is received, the sale is void because the condition of qabd before separation is lost.
This applies even if the guess turns out to be unequal.
5
Contrast with same-genre sale
If the same genus (e.g., gold for gold) is sold by guess, it is only valid if they know the items are equal before separation; otherwise it is invalid.
Equality in weight becomes a condition for same-genre sarf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو باع الذهب بالفضة مجازفة صح إن تقابضا في المجلس لأن المستحق هو القبض قبل الافتراق دون التسوية لما روينا فلا يضره الجزاف ولو افتراقا قبل قبضهما أو قبض أحدهما بطل لفوات الشرط قيد ببيع الجنس بخلاف الجنس لأنه لو باع الجنس بالجنس مجازفة فإن علما تساويهما قبل الافتراق صح وبعده لا . قوله : (ولا يصح التصرف في ثمن الصرف قبل قبضه فلو باع ديناراً بدراهم ثم اشتري الثوب كقولنا اهـ. قوله : (وقد نقل عن زفر الخ قال في فتح القدير : وهذا على إحدى الروايتين عنه أن النقود لا تتعين في البياعات فأما على الرواية الأخرى . عنه فيجب أن لا وبه اندفع ترجيح ابن الهمام الخ فيه نظر ظاهر فإن المحقق قد أجاب عن هذا وكان المؤلف لم يكمل يصح بيع
If one sells gold for silver by guess, it is valid if they exchange hand-to-hand in the session, because what is required is hand-to-hand delivery before separation, not equality, as we have narrated; so guess does not harm. If they separate before both are received or one is received, it becomes void due to the loss of the condition. This is restricted to selling one genus for another genus, because if he sells genus for genus by guess, if they know equality before separation it is valid, otherwise not. His statement: (And it is not valid to dispose of the price of sarf before its qabd, so if one sells a dinar for dirhams and then buys a cloth, like our saying. His statement: (And it has been narrated from Zufar) said in Fath al-Qadir: This is according to one of two narrations from him that currencies are not specified in sales. As for the other narration from him, then it must not... and with it the preference of Ibn al-Humam is repelled. But there is apparent consideration, for the investigator (al-Muhaqqiq) has answered this, and the author did not complete. The sale is not valid.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings: First, selling gold for silver by guess (mujazafah, without exact weight) is valid as long as the parties exchange the items hand-to-hand in the session, because only qabd before separation is required, not equality in weight. If they separate before receiving both or even one, the sale becomes void due to the loss of the condition. This applies only when selling one genus for another (gold for silver). If selling the same genus (gold for gold) by guess, it is valid only if they know the items are equal in weight before separation; otherwise it is not. Second, it is not valid to dispose of the price of sarf (e.g., the dirhams received) before taking possession. For example, if someone sells a dinar for dirhams and then uses those dirhams to buy a cloth, the purchase of the cloth is invalid. Then the passage mentions a narration from Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) regarding whether currencies are considered specific 'ayn in sales. There are two narrations from Zufar: one that they are not specified, and another that they are. The text ends abruptly with a note that Ibn al-Humam's preference was refuted by the investigator, but the author (of al-Bahr al-Raiq) did not complete the discussion.

Key Terms
مجازفة (mujāzafah): A sale by guess or estimation without exact measurement or weight.
قبض (qabd): Physical taking possession of the item being sold.
الصرف (al-ṣarf): The exchange of gold, silver, or currencies (ribawi items) for one another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is invalid because weight is unknown.
B) The sale is valid because qabd occurred.
C) The sale is invalid unless they know exact weight before separation.
D) The sale is valid only if they separate after qabd of both.

Key Takeaway
In sarf of different types, only hand-to-hand delivery in the session is required; guess is permissible.

Disposing of the Price Before Possession in Sarf and Zufar's Narration on Currency Specificity
Prohibition of spending the price before possession in sarf, and Zufar's narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that the price in a sarf transaction cannot be spent before qabd, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute about whether currencies are specific (a'yan) or fungible.

Core Idea
Spending the price of a sarf before taking possession invalidates the second purchase; Zufar's narration challenges this rule.

After a sarf exchange, the buyer receives the price (e.g., dirhams) but cannot use them until physically taking possession. This connects to a deeper theoretical issue: are currencies considered specific items (a'yan) or fungible? Zufar has two narrations; the relied-upon view is that currencies are not specific, so the prohibition stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sarf transaction
Scenario: selling a dinar (gold coin) for dirhams (silver coins). The dirhams are the price (thaman al-sarf).
This is a typical sarf exchange of different types.
2
Understand the prohibition
One cannot dispose of the price (e.g., use the dirhams to buy something else) before taking physical possession (qabd). Doing so invalidates the subsequent purchase.
The ruling is based on the hadith requiring hand-to-hand delivery.
3
Apply to a concrete example
If A sells a dinar to B for dirhams, and before B hands over the dirhams, A uses those dirhams to buy a cloth from B, the purchase of the cloth is invalid.
The price must be in A's possession before A can use it.
4
Explore Zufar's narration
Zufar has two narrations: (1) currencies are not specific (fungible) – the prohibition applies; (2) currencies are specific (a'yan) – which could change the ruling. The mufta bihi is the first narration.
The difference affects whether one can spend the price before qabd.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that currencies are not specified in sales, so the prohibition remains. Ibn al-Humam's preference for the second narration is repelled.
Fath al-Qadir indicates the first narration is the basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو باع الذهب بالفضة مجازفة صح إن تقابضا في المجلس لأن المستحق هو القبض قبل الافتراق دون التسوية لما روينا فلا يضره الجزاف ولو افتراقا قبل قبضهما أو قبض أحدهما بطل لفوات الشرط قيد ببيع الجنس بخلاف الجنس لأنه لو باع الجنس بالجنس مجازفة فإن علما تساويهما قبل الافتراق صح وبعده لا . قوله : (ولا يصح التصرف في ثمن الصرف قبل قبضه فلو باع ديناراً بدراهم ثم اشتري الثوب كقولنا اهـ. قوله : (وقد نقل عن زفر الخ قال في فتح القدير : وهذا على إحدى الروايتين عنه أن النقود لا تتعين في البياعات فأما على الرواية الأخرى . عنه فيجب أن لا وبه اندفع ترجيح ابن الهمام الخ فيه نظر ظاهر فإن المحقق قد أجاب عن هذا وكان المؤلف لم يكمل يصح بيع
If one sells gold for silver by guess, it is valid if they exchange hand-to-hand in the session, because what is required is hand-to-hand delivery before separation, not equality, as we have narrated; so guess does not harm. If they separate before both are received or one is received, it becomes void due to the loss of the condition. This is restricted to selling one genus for another genus, because if he sells genus for genus by guess, if they know equality before separation it is valid, otherwise not. His statement: (And it is not valid to dispose of the price of sarf before its qabd, so if one sells a dinar for dirhams and then buys a cloth, like our saying. His statement: (And it has been narrated from Zufar) said in Fath al-Qadir: This is according to one of two narrations from him that currencies are not specified in sales. As for the other narration from him, then it must not... and with it the preference of Ibn al-Humam is repelled. But there is apparent consideration, for the investigator (al-Muhaqqiq) has answered this, and the author did not complete. The sale is not valid.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings: First, selling gold for silver by guess (mujazafah, without exact weight) is valid as long as the parties exchange the items hand-to-hand in the session, because only qabd before separation is required, not equality in weight. If they separate before receiving both or even one, the sale becomes void due to the loss of the condition. This applies only when selling one genus for another (gold for silver). If selling the same genus (gold for gold) by guess, it is valid only if they know the items are equal in weight before separation; otherwise it is not. Second, it is not valid to dispose of the price of sarf (e.g., the dirhams received) before taking possession. For example, if someone sells a dinar for dirhams and then uses those dirhams to buy a cloth, the purchase of the cloth is invalid. Then the passage mentions a narration from Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) regarding whether currencies are considered specific 'ayn in sales. There are two narrations from Zufar: one that they are not specified, and another that they are. The text ends abruptly with a note that Ibn al-Humam's preference was refuted by the investigator, but the author (of al-Bahr al-Raiq) did not complete the discussion.

Key Terms
ثمن الصرف (thaman al-ṣarf): The price received in a sarf transaction, e.g., the dirhams received in exchange for a dinar.
لا تتعين النقود (lā tata'ayyan al-nuqūd): Currencies are not considered specific 'ayn (individual items) in sales; they are fungible.
مندفع (mundafi'): Repelled or pushed back; used here to indicate that Ibn al-Humam's preference is set aside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using the dirhams received from selling a dinar to buy something else before taking possession of the dirhams?
A) Valid, because ownership transfers immediately.
B) Invalid, because the price must be received first.
C) Valid, only if the purchase is also hand-to-hand.
D) Invalid, only if the dinar was also not received.

Key Takeaway
The price in a sarf transaction cannot be spent before physical possession; the relied-upon view treats currencies as fungible, not specific.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
The Invalidity of Using Unreceived Sarf Currency in Another Sale
Commentary on sarf rulings with expansion on combined sales and istibdal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on buying a garment with dirhams that are the price in a sarf contract before receipt, and explain why the sale is fasid, including the difference with Imam Zufar's view.

Core Idea
Sarf currency must be received before use; using it in another sale is fasid because it violates a divine right.

This lesson analyzes a key scenario in sarf: a person sells a dinar for ten dirhams and then buys a garment with those dirhams before receiving them. The Hanafi school rules the garment sale invalid (fasid). We will examine the reasoning, the divine right argument, and a minority intra-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contracts
Recognize that there are two separate contracts: a sarf contract (dinar for ten dirhams) and a subsequent garment sale using those same dirhams as price.
The dirhams are both the subject of the sarf and the price in the garment sale.
2
Apply the sarf condition of qabd
In sarf, possession of both currencies must occur in the same session (majlis) as a condition of validity. This is a right of Allah, not waivable by the parties.
The dirhams have not been received yet; thus the sarf remains pending.
3
Determine the effect on the garment sale
Using those unreceived dirhams as the price in another sale creates a condition that contradicts the required qabd. This condition is fasid, making the garment sale itself fasid.
Fasid means invalid due to a defect, not void (batil) from the start.
4
Consider the Zufar objection
Imam Zufar argues that the dirhams in the garment sale are not specifically earmarked as the sarf price, so the sale can be valid. The majority rejects this because the intention to pay from those dirhams effectively ties them.
The Hanafi tarjih upholds the invalidity, as per the author and Fath al-Qadir.
5
Apply the ruling to analogous cases
The same principle applies to any sale before possession in sarf, such as buying a measurable commodity with unreceived sarf currency. Later cases in the text (necklace, sword) illustrate similar reasoning.
The focus remains on the necessity of qabd before using the currency.

بها ثوباً فسد البيع في الثوب أي في أحد بدلي الصرف لأن كلاً منهما ثمن فلا تجوز هبته ولا صدقته ولا بيع شيء به، وقدمنا أنه إن وهب أو تصدق به أو أبرأه فإن قبل الآخر انفسخ الصرف لتعذر وجود القبض وإلا فلا. وأما البيع فصورته كما ذكره المصنف باع ديناراً بعشرة دراهم ولم يقبضها حتى اشترى بها ثوباً أو مكيلاً أو موزوناً فالبيع في الثوب فاسد لأن قبض العشرة مستحق حقاً الله تعالى فلا يسقط بإسقاط المتعاقدين فلم يجز بيع الثوب والصرف على حاله يقبض بدله من عاقده معه . وأورد عليه أن فساد الصرف حينئذ حق الله تعالى وصحة الثوب حق العبد فتعارضا فيقدم حق العبد لتفضل الله بذلك. وأجيب بأن ذلك بعد ثبوت الحقين ولم يثبت حق العبد بعد لأنه يفوت حق الله بعد تحققه فيمتنع لا أنه يرتفع، وقد نقل عن زفر صحة بيع الثوب لأن الثمن في بيعه لم يتعين كونه بدل الصرف لأن العقد لا يتعين فإضافة العقد إلى بدل الصرف كعدم إضافته فيجوز شراء ثوب بدراهم لم يصفها. وجوابه أن قبض بدل الصرف واجب والاستبدال يفوته فكان شرط إيفاء ثمن الثوب من بدل الصرف شرطاً فاسداً فيمتنع الجواز وقد رجحه في فتح القدير. ثم اعلم أنهم قرروا هنا كما في المعراج أن البدلين في باب الصرف كل منهما ثمن قبل العقد وحالته فلا يشترط وجودها

في ملك المتصارفين ولا يتعينان ،بالإشارة ومثمن من وجه بعد العقد ضرورة أن العقد لا له من مثمن فلا يجوز الاستبدال بأحدهما قبل القبض لكونه بيع المبيع قبل قبضه إلى آخره، وبه اندفع ترجيح ابن الهمام قول زفر كما لا يخفى. وفي الذخيرة إذا اشترى الرجل ألف درهم بعينها بمائة دينار والدراهم بيض فأعطاه مكانها سوداً ورضي بها البائع جاز ذلك لأن هذا ليس باستبدال والسود والبيض من الدراهم جنس واحد، وإنما أبرأه عن صفة الجودة حين تجوز بالسود فكان مستوفياً بهذه الطريق لا مستبدلاً . قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي: ومراده من السود الدراهم المضروبة من النقود السود لا الدراهم البخارية لأن أخذ البخارية مكان الدراهم البيض لا يجوز لأنه يكون استبدالاً لاختلاف الجنس. وكذلك لو قبض مشتري الدراهم الدراهم فأراد أن يعطي ضرباً آخر من الدنانير سوى ما شرط لا يجوز إلا برضا صاحبه وإذا رضي به صاحبه كان مستوفياً لا مستبدلاً لكون الجنس واحداً. قيل : هذا إذا أعطى ضرباً دون المسمى، فأما إذا أعطاه ضرباً فوق المسمى فلا حاجة إلى رضا صاحبه اهـ . وقدمنا جواز الرهن ببدل الصرف فإن هلك وهما في المجلس هلك بما فيه وجاز العقد، وإن
النظر في عبارته، ثم رأيت صاحب النهر لخص جواب المحقق واعترض كلام المؤلف حيث قال : ولا يخفى أن زفر إنما قال يجوز البيع بناء على عدم تعين بدل الصرف ثمناً فجاز أن يعطي من غيره، ولا شك أنه يقول بعدم جواز بيع المبيع قبل القبض فإذا قال بصحة هذا البيع لما قلنا كان بالضرورة قائلاً بأن البيع انعقد موجباً دفع مثله وتكون تسميته بدل الصرف تقديراً للثمن، سواء سميته بيعاً أو

مطلقاً
The Book of Currency Exchange (Sarf). ... (full translation would be lengthy; here summarized) ...
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe on the rulings of sarf. The author discusses several scenarios. First: if someone sells a dinar for ten dirhams and then buys a garment with those dirhams before receiving them, the garment sale is fasid (invalid) because the dirhams are one of the two currencies in the sarf contract and must be received in the majlis. The obligation to receive is a right of Allah, not waivable by the parties. A dispute with Zufar is noted: Zufar allows the garment sale because the dirham are not specifically earmarked for the sarf. The author rejects this, relying on the obligation of qabd. Second: if one buys specified white dirhams for dinars, then gives black dirhams instead, it is valid if the seller agrees, as it is not an istibdal (substitution) but taking possession of the same genus. Third: selling a slave girl with a necklace: if part of the price is paid cash and part on credit, the cash portion is considered for the necklace (which is a sarf item) because immediate possession is required. Fourth: selling a sword with a hilt: if the price is paid partially, that portion is for the hilt. The commentary emphasizes that in sarf, both currencies are considered prices, and prior possession is essential.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): The exchange of gold for silver or silver for gold, or of the same genus by weight/measure, requiring hand-to-hand possession.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession (or constructive possession) of the exchanged item in the same session for the validity of the sarf.
استبدال (istibdal): Substituting one currency for another before taking possession, which is prohibited in sarf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person sells a dinar for ten dirhams and then buys a garment with those dirhams before receiving them, what is the ruling on the garment sale?
A) Valid (sahih)
B) Invalid (fasid)
C) Batil (void)
D) Permissible (ja'iz)

Key Takeaway
In sarf, currency must be received hand-to-hand before it can be used in any other transaction; otherwise, the subsequent sale is fasid.

Payment Allocation in Composite Sale of Sword with Silver Fittings
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specification of payment in a sarf-non-sarf composite contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on payment specification in a composite sale and state the reconciled mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The explicit word 'specifically' invalidates the sarf component; ambiguity saves the contract.

In a sale combining a sarf element (silver fittings) and a non-sarf element (sword), the buyer's verbal allocation of payment can affect validity. The Hanafi school has a nuanced discussion on whether specifying payment to the non-sarf part invalidates the sarf part. This lesson unpacks the key rulings from Al-Mabsut and Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and the commentator's reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components
Recognize that the sale involves both a sarf component (silver hilya) and a non-sarf component (sword blade/scabbard). The payment is in dirhams, which can be allocated to either.
The hilya is the silver ornament; the sword is the rest.
2
Default attribution rule
Understand that in a composite sale, the payment is automatically attributed to the sarf component (hilya) unless the buyer explicitly states otherwise.
This is based on istihsan and the need to preserve the sarf exchange.
3
Explicit specification case
Analyze the ruling from Al-Mabsut: if the buyer says 'Take these fifty from the price of the sword specifically' (with the word 'خاصة'), and they part, the sale of the hilya is invalidated because the attribution to the hilya is removed.
The word 'خاصة' is key; it eliminates ambiguity.
4
Ambiguous wording case
Examine the ruling from Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if the buyer says 'This is from the price of the sword' without 'specifically', the payment is still considered for the hilya and the sale is valid, because the term 'sword' includes the hilya as a subsidiary.
Here, the ambiguity allows the payment to be attributed to the hilya.
5
Reconciliation and fatwa
Note the commentator's reconciliation: Al-Mabsut's ruling applies only when 'specifically' (خاصة) is used; otherwise, the view of Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj prevails. The mufta bihi is that without 'specifically', the sale is valid.
This preserves contracts and avoids riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصرف
وفي الحديث «فأذنا وأقيما» والمراد أحدهما فيحمل عليه لظاهر حالهما بالإسلام. ونظيره في الفقه إذا حضتما حيضة أو ولدتما ولداً علق بأحدهما للاستحالة بخلاف ما إذا لم يذكر المفعول به للإمكان. وقد فاته صورتان الأولى أن يبين ويقول خذ هذا نصفه من ثمن الحلية ونصفه من ثمن السيف. الثانية أن يجعل الكل من ثمن السيف وفيهما يكون المقبوض ثمن الحلية لأنهما شيء واحد فيجعل عن الحلية الحصول مراده ؛ هكذا ذكره الشارح. وفي المعراج معزياً إلى المبسوط : لو قال خذ هذه الخمسين من ثمن السيف خاصة وقال الآخر نعم أو قال لا وتفرقا على ذلك انتقض البيع في الحلية لأن الترجيح بالاستحقاق عند المساواة في العقد أو الإضافة، ولا مساواة بعد تصريح الدافع بكون المدفوع ثمن السيف خاصة والقول في ذلك وقوله لأنه هو الملك فالقول له في بيان جهته اهـ وهكذا في العناية. وفي السراج الوهاج : ولو قال هذا الذي عجلته حصة السيف كان عن الحلية وجاز البيع لأن السيف اسم للحلية أيضاً لأنها تدخل في بيعه تبعاً. ولو قال هذا من ثمن الجفن والنصل خاصة فسد البيع لأنه بذلك وأزال الاحتمال فلم يمكن حمله على الصحة اهـ. ويمكن التوفيق بأن يحمل ما ذكره الشارح على ما إذا قال من ثمن السيف ولم يقل خاصة فيوافق ما في السراج الوهاج.
صرح
yصلح دفعاً حذفناه خوف الإطالة بلا فائدة قوله : (وفي المعراج معزياً إلى المبسوط الخ) أقول وفي كافي الحاكم : وإذا اشترى قلباً بعشرة دراهم وفيه عشرة دراهم وقبض القلب وغصبه الآخر عشرة دراهم ثم افترقا فهي قصاص بثمن القلب وإن تفرقا على غير رضا وكذلك القرض، ولو اشترى القلب مع ثوب بعشرين درهماً وقبض القلب ونقده عشرة دراهم ثم تفرقاً جعلت ما نقده ثمن القلب استحساناً، ولو نقده العشرة فقال هي من ثمنهما جميعاً فهو مثل الأول، فإن قال من ثمن الثوب خاصة وقال الآخر نعم أو قال لا وتفرقا على ذلك انتقض البيع في القلب لأن الدافع يجعلها قضاء من أيهما شاء، وكذلك لو كان الثمن ديناراً، وكذلك لو اشترى سيفاً محلى بمائة درهم وحليته خمسون درهماً فقبض السيف ونقده خمسين درهماً وقال هي من ثمن السيف أو قال من ثمن السيف والحلية أو من ثمن السيف دون الحلية ورضي بذلك القابض أو لم يرض فهو سواء والذي نقد من ثمن الحلية استحساناً اهـ وانظر ما الفرق بين قوله ثمن الثوب خاصة وقوله من ثمن السيف دون الحلية

And in Al-Mi'raj quoting Al-Mabsut: if he said 'Take these fifty specifically from the price of the sword' and the other said yes, or said no and they separated on that, the sale of the hilya is invalidated because weighting by entitlement requires equality in the contract or attribution, and there is no equality after the payer has declared that the paid amount is specifically the price of the sword. The statement regarding that and his statement 'because he is the owner' means the statement is his in explaining its direction. End quotation. Similarly in Al-Inaya. And in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if he said 'This which I have expedited is the share of the sword', it is considered for the hilya and the sale is valid because the sword is also a name for the hilya since it enters its sale as a subsidiary. And if he said 'This is from the price of the scabbard and blade specifically', the sale becomes invalid because he thereby removes the possibility and it cannot be interpreted as valid. End. Reconciliation is possible by taking what the commentator mentioned as the case when he said 'from the price of the sword' without saying 'specifically', so it agrees with what is in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj... Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of payment in a composite contract involving both a sarf (currency exchange) component and a non-sarf component, specifically the sale of a sword adorned with silver fittings (hilya). The central issue: when the buyer pays a sum in silver dirhams and verbally allocates the payment to only one part of the item (e.g., the blade or the hilya), does that specification affect the validity of the entire contract? The author of the sharh begins by noting two scenarios missed by the matn: (1) the buyer explicitly says 'take half from the price of the hilya and half from the price of the sword'; (2) he says 'all from the price of the sword.' In both, the received dirhams are considered the price of the hilya, because the sword and hilya are treated as a single unit for the purpose of sarf; the buyer's intention is fulfilled by attributing the payment to the hilya. Then the text brings a key ruling from Al-Mabsut via Al-Mi'raj: if the buyer says 'take these fifty specifically from the price of the sword' and the seller agrees or disagrees and they part, the sale of the hilya is invalidated. The reason is that once the payer explicitly restricts the payment to the sword (the non-sarf part), the natural association of the payment with the hilya is broken, and since the hilya is the locus of the sarf obligation, its sale is invalid. However, Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj offers a different view: if the buyer says 'this is the share of the sword,' it is valid and considered as paid for the hilya because the term 'sword' includes the hilya by way of subsidiary inclusion. But if he specifies 'from the price of the scabbard and blade only,' the sale becomes invalid (fasid) because the possibility of interpretation is removed. The author reconciles these by saying the earlier commentator's ruling applies when the buyer says 'from the price of the sword' without the word 'specifically,' which then aligns with Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The text then discusses a parallel from Al-Kafi involving a heart (qalb) of silver and a garment (thawb), highlighting a distinction: specifying 'from the price of the garment only' invalidates the sale of the heart, whereas specifying 'from the price of the sword without the hilya' does not invalidate, because the sword cannot be free of the hilya without damage. The author also examines the requirement of reciprocal payment (qabd) before parting, noting that if they separate without full payment, the sarf part is invalid, and the non-sarf part is valid only if it can be separated without harm. Finally, the passage extends to gilded items (mumawwah), where the gold/silver is considered consumed (mustahlikah) and thus not subject to sarf rules unless the quantity is significant. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) from Al-Mabsut is to avoid selling such items with like metal; it is preferable to sell with a different metal to avoid riba.

Key Terms
الحلية (al-hilyah): The silver ornament or fittings on a sword, which in the context of sarf is considered a separate substance of silver subject to currency exchange rules.
السيف (al-sayf): The sword itself, including its blade and hilt, but in this context used to refer to the non-sarf component (the blade and scabbard) as opposed to the silver hilya.
التمويه (al-tamwīh): Gilding or plating with gold or silver in a thin layer that is consumed and cannot be separated, thus not considered a separate substance for riba purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of a sword with silver fittings (hilya) for 100 dirhams, if the buyer pays 50 dirhams and says 'I give these 50 specifically from the price of the sword' (خاصة), and they part, what is the ruling on the sale of the hilya according to Al-Mabsut?
A) The sale of the hilya is invalid (ينتقض البيع في الحلية).
B) The sale of the hilya is valid because the sword includes the hilya.
C) The entire sale is invalid (بطل العقد كله).
D) The sale of the hilya is suspended until the buyer clarifies.

Key Takeaway
In composite sales with a sarf component, ambiguous payment allocation is interpreted in favor of the hilya; explicit specification to the non-sarf part invalidates the sarf contract.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Selling a Composite Item in Currency Exchange: The Basic Ruling
Explains the ruling on a composite item in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on selling a composite item (e.g., sword with silver hilt) in a sarf transaction by identifying when the sale is valid or invalid based on separability and qabd.

Core Idea
If the ornament can be removed without harm, only its sale is invalid without qabd; the rest remains valid.

When a commodity combines a metal subject to riba rules with a non-metal item, the sarf conditions apply only to the metal part. This lesson unpacks the foundational ruling from al-Bahr al-Raiq on a sword with a silver hilt, using the classic analogy of a slave girl with a necklace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a sword with a silver hilt for silver currency. The ruling is that the sale of the hilt (subject to sarf) requires qabd before separation; the blade does not.
2
Locate the condition
The key condition is takhallus: can the ornament be removed without damaging the main item?
3
Apply the qiyas
The analogy with a slave girl and a detachable necklace: if the necklace can be removed, its sale is invalid without qabd, but the slave girl's sale remains valid.
This shows the principle of separability.
4
Note the price conditions
If the price is less than or equal to the ornament's weight, or unknown, the sale is invalid due to riba; only if the price is known to be greater does the sale become valid.
Three invalid cases, one valid.
5
Distinguish different-type case
If the price is of a different metal (e.g., gold for silver), sarf does not apply, and the sale is permissible in any amount.
Disparity is allowed between different types.

وأما السيف إذا سمي فقال نصفها من ثمن الحلية ونصفها من ثمن نصل السيف ثم تفرقا لم يفسد البيع اهـ. ولذا قال الزيلعي لأنهما شيء واحد قوله : (جاز كيفما كان) أي سواء كان المدفوع مساوياً لقيمة الحلية أو لوزنها أو لا، ولا لجواز التفاضل عند اختلاف الجنس، ومقتضى هذا أنه يصرف المدفوع إلى الحلية فيكون ثمناً لها ويكون باقي الثمن وهو غير المدفوع ثمن النصل. قوله : هذا بيع المزركش والمطرز (الخ قال الرملي في حاشية المنح قال في مجمع الرواية بعد أن ذكر مسألة حلية السيف ناقلاً عن المحيط : وإن كان مموهاً جاز مطلقاً لأن الفضة بالتمويه صارت مستهلكة لأنها لا تخلص بعد التمويه ولكن بقي لونها ألا ترى لو اشترى داراً مموهاً بالذهب بذهب مؤجل يجوز ولو بقي عين الذهب لوجب أن لا يجوز اهـ وأقول : المموه المطلي بالذهب أو الفضة، والتمويه الطلي مأخوذ من تمويه الكلام أي تلبيسه وأقول : يجب تقييد المسألة بما إذا لم تكثر الفضة أو الذهب المموه أما إذا كثر بحيث يحصل منه شيء يدخل في الميزان بالعرض على النار يجب حينئذ اعتباره، ولم أره لأصحابنا لكن رأيته للشافعية وقواعدنا شاهدة به فتأمل والله تعالى أعلم .اهـ. قلت: وسيأتي عند قول المتن وغالب الغش ليس في حكم الدراهم والدنانير» ما هو كالصريح في ذلك فتأمل. وفي كافي الحاكم : وإذا اشترى لجاماً مموهاً بفضة بدراهم أقل مما فيه أو أكثر فهو جائز لأن التمويه لا يخلص ألا ترى أنه إذا اشترى الدار المموهة بالذهب بثمن مؤجل يجوز ذلك وإن كان ما في سقوفها من التمويه
أن تكون هذه كالمسألة المتقدمة أنه يصرف إلى الحلية ومن أنه على التفصيل المتقدم ذكره من يعني إن كان الحلية تتخلص بغير ضرر صح في السيف خاصة وإلا بطل في الكل. وفي المحيط : لو قال هذا من ثمن النصل خاصة فإن لم يمكن التمييز إلا بضرر يكون المنقود ثمن الصرف ويصحان جميعاً لأنه قصد صحة البيع ولا صحة له إلا بصرف المنقود إلى الصرف فحكمنا بجوازه تصحيحاً للبيع، وإن أمكن تمييزها بغير ضرر بطل الصرف، فعلى هذا ما ذكر في المبسوط محمول على ما إذا كانت الحلية تتخلص من غير ضرر توفيقاً بينه وبين ما ذكر في المحيط اهـ. وفيه نظر لأن ما في المحيط إنما هو فيما إذا صرح بالنصل دون السيف، ولا شك في عدم انصرافه إلى الحلية لأنه كما قدمناه لكن بشرط أن يتخلص بلا ضرر وإلا صریح صرفناها إلى الحلية، وتركنا الصريح تصحيحاً لأنه لولا ذلك بطل في الكل، وما في المبسوط إنما هو فيما إذا قال خذ هذا من ثمن السيف خاصة فذكر السيف ولم يذكر النصل . والحاصل أنه إن ذكر السيف ولم يقل خاصة صرف إلى الحلية مطلقاً أعني سواء أمكن التمييز بلا ضرر أو لا، وإن زاد خاصة أو لم يذكر السيف وإنما ذكر النصل لا ينصرف إليها ويصرف إلى النصل إن أمكن تخليصه بلا ضرر وإلا صرفناه إلى الحلية. وفي البدائع : إن ذكر أنه من ثمن السيف يقع عن الحلية، وإن ذكر أنه من ثمن النصل فإن أمكن تخليصه بلا ضرر يقع عن المذكور ويبطل الصرف بالافتراق وإلا فالمنقود ثمن الصرف ويصحان اهـ. وفي المغرب: الحلية الزينة من ذهب أو فضة يقال حلية السيف والسرج وغيره. وفي التنزيل وتستخرجون حلية تلبسونها [فاطر: ۱۲] أي اللؤلؤ والمرجان اهـ
If they separate without qabd, it is valid for the sword but not for the ornament if it can be removed without harm; otherwise both are invalid. As for what is in al-Mabsut, it said 'specifically' and then it is as if he said 'take this for the blade'. He restricted it to one hundred because if he sold it for fifty or less, riba does not occur; if he sold it for silver whose weight is unknown, it is also not permissible due to the suspicion of riba. There are three cases where the sale is invalid, and one where it is valid: when the price is known to exceed the ornament so that the equivalent of the ornament is for it and the rest for the blade. This applies when the price is of the same type as the ornament; if of a different type, it is permissible in any case due to the permissibility of disparity. The ornament has no specificity with the sword or the necklace with the slave girl; rather the point is when combining sarf with something else. For the currency does not cease being sarf by association. On this is the sale of embroidered and decorated items with gold or silver. In al-Mabsut: Ibn Sirin disliked selling it with its own type, and we adopt that due to the possibility of excess, but it is better to sell it with a different type. His statement: (If they separate without qabd, it is valid for the sword but not for the ornament if it can be removed without harm; otherwise both are invalid) means the contract is invalid for both because the share of sarf must be taken before separation; if he did not take possession until they separated, it becomes invalid due to the absence of its condition. Likewise for the sword if it cannot be removed except with harm, due to the impossibility of delivery without harm, like selling a beam from a roof. If it can be removed without harm, it is valid due to the ability to deliver, and it becomes like the slave girl with the necklace. The commentator mentioned here what we narrated from al-Mabsut previously. The seeker of his Lord's pardon said: It is appropriate... And the sword if he specified and said: half is from the price of the ornament and half from the price of the blade, then they separated, the sale is not invalid. Hence al-Zayla'i said: because they are one thing. His statement: (Permissible in any case) means whether the amount paid equals the value or weight of the ornament or not, due to the permissibility of disparity when the types differ. The implication is that the amount paid is allocated to the ornament and becomes its price, and the remainder is the price of the blade. His statement: This is the sale of embroidered and decorated items... Al-Ramli said in Hashiyat al-Minhaj: In Majma' al-Riwayah, after mentioning the issue of the sword's ornament, quoting from al-Muhit: If it is gilded (mumawwah), it is permissible absolutely because the silver through gilding becomes consumed as it cannot be extracted after gilding, though its color remains. Do you not see that if one buys a house gilded with gold for deferred payment, it is permissible; if the gold substance remained, it would not be permissible. The gilded (mumawwah) is the one plated with gold or silver, and gilding (tamwiyah) is coating. It is necessary to restrict the issue to when the plated metal is not abundant; if abundant so that it can be obtained by fire, then it must be considered. I have not seen this from our scholars, but I saw it from the Shafi'is, and our principles testify to it. I say: It will come later when the text says 'and most of the adulteration is not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars' what is clear in that. In Kafi al-Hakim: If one buys a bridle gilded with silver for dirhams less or more, it is permissible because the gilding does not extract. Do you not see that if he buys a house gilded with gold for deferred payment, it is permissible, even if what is in its ceilings of gilding... This is like the previous issue: it is allocated to the ornament, and that it is according to the earlier detailed discussion: if the ornament can be removed without harm, it is valid for the sword specifically; otherwise it is invalid for all. In al-Muhit: If he said 'this is from the price of the blade specifically' and it cannot be distinguished except with harm, the amount paid is for the sarf and both are valid because he intended the validity of the sale, and there is no validity except by allocating the amount to the sarf, so we rule it permissible to validate the sale. If it can be distinguished without harm, the sarf is invalid. Accordingly, what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is construed as when the ornament can be removed without harm, to reconcile between it and what is mentioned in al-Muhit. There is a consideration because what is in al-Muhit is only when he specifies the blade without the sword, and there is no doubt that it does not apply to the ornament, as we presented, but on condition that it can be removed without harm; otherwise we allocate it to the ornament and abandon the explicit wording to validate, because otherwise the whole would be invalid. And what is in al-Mabsut is only when he says 'take this from the price of the sword specifically,' so he mentioned the sword and did not mention the blade. The upshot: If he mentions the sword and does not say 'specifically', it is allocated to the ornament absolutely, i.e., whether the removal can be done without harm or not. If he adds 'specifically' or does not mention the sword but only mentions the blade, it is not allocated to the ornament, and it is allocated to the blade if it can be extracted without harm; otherwise we allocate it to the ornament. In al-Bada'i: If he mentions that it is from the price of the sword, it applies to the ornament; if he mentions that it is from the price of the blade, then if it can be extracted without harm, it applies to the mentioned and the sarf is invalid by separation; otherwise the amount paid is for the sarf and both are valid. In al-Mughrib: Al-hilya (ornament) is decoration from gold or silver; one says hilyat al-sayf (ornament of the sword) and the like. In the Quran: 'and you extract ornaments that you wear' [35:12], meaning pearls and coral.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, addressing the ruling of selling a composite item—such as a sword with a silver hilt—in a transaction involving currency exchange (sarf). The core issue is that when the price is of the same metal as the ornament (e.g., silver for a silver hilt), the rules of sarf apply: both parties must take possession (qabd) before separating. If they separate without taking possession of the metal portion, the sale of that portion is invalid. However, if the ornament can be removed from the sword without causing damage, the sale of the sword itself remains valid because it is not subject to sarf. If removal causes harm (e.g., cutting the sword), the entire sale becomes invalid due to impossibility of delivery.

The text then discusses cases where the price is explicitly allocated to the blade or the sword. If the buyer says 'this is from the price of the blade' and the blade can be removed easily, the payment is for the blade and the sarf is invalid due to non-possession. If removal is difficult, the payment is considered for the ornament (the metal part) to validate the sarf, and the whole sale becomes valid—this is a principle of validating transactions when possible.

A key disagreement arises between two authoritative sources: al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. Al-Mabsut holds that if the buyer says 'take this from the price of the sword specifically,' the payment is allocated to the ornament (the silver hilt) unconditionally. Al-Muhit holds that if he says 'from the price of the blade,' the payment goes to the blade if separable without harm; otherwise it goes to the ornament. The commentator reconciles them by saying al-Mabsut's case is when the sword is mentioned without 'specifically,' while al-Muhit's case is when the blade is mentioned. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that mentioning the sword without qualification allocates the payment to the ornament absolutely; mentioning the blade allocates to the blade only if separable without harm; otherwise it goes to the ornament to preserve the validity of the sale.

The text also extends the ruling to plated items (mumawwah): if gold or silver is used as a thin plating that cannot be recovered, the transaction is considered a sale of the item itself, not of the metal, and thus sarf rules do not apply. However, if the plating is thick enough to be extracted, it must be treated as a mixed transaction.

Key Terms
حلية (hilya): Ornament or decoration made of gold or silver attached to an item like a sword, necklace, etc.
صرف (sarf): Currency exchange; the sale of gold for gold, silver for silver, or both, with immediate possession and equality in weight if same type.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the item being sold; in sarf, it is a condition for validity.
تخلص (takhallus): The ability to remove or extract the ornament from the sword or item without causing damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sword with a silver hilt is sold for 100 silver dirhams. The hilt can be removed without damage. They separate without qabd. What is the ruling?
A) The entire sale is invalid.
B) The sale of the blade is valid; the hilt sale is invalid.
C) The sale of the hilt is valid; the blade sale is invalid.
D) The sale is valid for both.

Key Takeaway
In a composite item, the metal portion subject to sarf requires qabd before separation; if separable without harm, only that portion is invalidated by its absence.

Buyer's Option When Part of a Jointly-Owned Vessel Is Claimed
Commentary expanding a ruling on buyer's option when part of a vessel is claimed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a buyer may keep the remainder of a jointly-owned vessel by paying a proportionate price, or return it, and identify when the contract is void due to separation before the claimant's ratification.

Core Idea
Joint ownership in a vessel is a defect giving the buyer khiyar al-‘ayb—the option is absolute and applies even after delivery.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq expands a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa’iq on a common sale scenario: a buyer purchases a vessel (a pot or container) that later turns out to be partly owned by a third party. The Hanafi school treats this partial ownership as a defect (ʿayb) because dividing the vessel harms its utility. The buyer therefore has an option: keep the remainder at a reduced price or cancel the sale entirely. However, the outcome depends on whether the rightful claimant ratifies the sale, and crucially, on whether the buyer and seller have separated from the contract session before ratification. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the conditions that determine whether the contract is valid or void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
The passage states: if part of a vessel is rightfully claimed, the buyer may either take the remaining part by paying its proportionate price (bi-qistihi) or return the entire sale. State this clearly.
The option is given because joint ownership is a defect—this is the proof (ta'lil) based on harm from division.
2
Explain the Legal Basis (ʿIllah)
The reason (ʿillah) for the option is that joint ownership (shirkah) in a vessel is a defect; dividing it (taqṣīṣ) harms its utility. This defect existed at the time of sale, so it triggers khiyar al-ʿayb (option of defect). Confirm that the buyer has a right to cancel or demand a proportional reduction.
This is the 'talil' argument type—the defect is not in the item's physical condition but in the legal status.
3
Analyze the Effect of the Claimant's Ratification
If the rightful claimant ratifies the sale before a court ruling, the contract becomes valid. The price then belongs to the claimant, and the seller acts as his agent to collect it from the buyer. However, the contract's rights (like khiyar) are attached to the agent (seller), not the claimant. Detail the consequences.
Ratification must occur while buyer and seller are still together in the contract session (majlis al-ʿaqd).
4
Identify When the Contract Becomes Void
The contract is void (bāṭil) in two scenarios: (a) if the buyer and seller separate from the contract session before the claimant ratifies; (b) if the claimant leaves the session before ratifying while buyer and seller remain. Understand that separation severs the possibility of ratification.
This is based on the principle that ratification must happen in the same session; otherwise the contract is nullified.
5
Determine the Scope of the Option
The commentator notes that the option (al-khiyār) is absolute (muṭlaq), applying both before and after the buyer takes possession (qabḍ). This means even after delivery, if the defect is discovered, the buyer may still exercise the option.
This counters a potential misunderstanding that the option ends after delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استحق بعض الإناء أخذ المشتري ما بقي بقسطه أو رد) لأن الشركة في الإناء عيب لأن التشقيص يضره وهذا العيب كان موجوداً عند البائع مقارناً له، فإن أجاز المستحق قبل أن يحكم له بالاستحقاق جاز العقد وكان الثمن له يأخذه البائع من المشتري ويسلمه إليه إذا لم يفترقا بعد الإجازة ويصير العاقد وكيلاً للمجيز فتتعلق حقوق العقد بالوكيل دون المجيز حتى لو افترق المتعاقدان قبل إجازة المستحق بطل العقد. وإن فارقه المستحق قبل الإجازة والمتعاقدان باقيان في المجلس بطل العقد؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. أطلق الخيار فشمل ما قبل القبض وبعده.
And if some of the vessel is rightfully claimed, the buyer takes what remains by its proportion or he returns [the sale] because joint ownership in the vessel is a defect since division harms it, and this defect existed with the seller concurrent with him. If the rightful claimant ratifies before a ruling is given for the claim, the contract becomes valid, and the price belongs to him, the seller takes it from the buyer and delivers it to him if they have not separated after the ratification, and the two contracting parties become agents for the rater; so the rights of the contract are attached to the agent, not the rater, to the extent that if the two contracting parties separate before the ratification of the rightful claimant, the contract is void. And if the rightful claimant leaves before ratification while the two contracting parties remain in the session, the contract is void; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. He made the option absolute, so it includes before and after taking possession.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining a ruling from the matn: when a sold vessel is partially owned by someone else, and that person claims his share (istihqaq), the buyer has an option: either keep the remainder by paying a proportionate part of the price, or cancel the sale entirely. The reason given is that joint ownership (shirkah) in a vessel is a defect, because dividing a vessel harms its utility. This defect existed at the time of sale, so the buyer has the khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect). The author then explains the effect of the rightful claimant's ratification: if he ratifies before a court ruling, the contract becomes valid, the claimant takes the entire price (since the seller had no right to sell the claimant's share), and the seller acts as his agent to receive the price from the buyer. The contract's rights (like option of defect) are then between the buyer and the agent (seller), not the claimant. However, if the buyer and seller separate (i.e., leave the session) before the claimant ratifies, the contract becomes void because the ratification did not occur while the parties were together. Similarly, if the claimant leaves the session before ratifying while buyer and seller remain, the contract also becomes void. The commentator notes that in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the option (al-khiyar) is described as absolute (mutlaq), meaning it applies both before and after taking possession. This is important because in other contracts, when the sold item is partially destroyed before delivery, the buyer may have a different option. Here, because the defect (shirkah) existed from the outset, the option persists even after delivery.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqāq): The right of a third party to claim ownership of part of the sold item, established by proof.
خيار (khiyār): An option granted to the buyer to either cancel the sale or keep the item with a price adjustment, due to a defect.
تشقيص (taqṣīṣ): The act of dividing the vessel into parts, which would harm its utility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer purchases a vessel that is later found to be partially owned by a third party (istihqaq), what options does the buyer have according to this passage?
A) The buyer must return the entire vessel and get a full refund.
B) The buyer may take the remainder by paying a proportionate price or return the vessel.
C) The buyer must take the remainder and pay the full price.
D) The buyer has no option and must complete the sale.

Key Takeaway
When part of a sold item is rightfully claimed by a third party, the Hanafi school gives the buyer an option to keep the remainder pro rata or rescind, contingent on the claimant's ratification and the session's continuity.

Principle of Dividing Consideration in Sales
Presenting the general principle from al-Idah on how to apportion consideration in sales involving multiple items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for dividing consideration in a sale with multiple items, distinguishing between non-riba and riba cases.

Core Idea
In mixed sales, divide by parts if uniform, by value if variable, by riba-validation if ribawi.

This passage from al-Idah presents a general principle for apportioning consideration when both sides of a sale contain multiple items. The correct division is crucial for the contract's validity, especially in riba-prone transactions. Understanding this rule will help you determine the proper method for different types of goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sale type
Determine if the items involved are ribawi (gold, silver, foodgrain) or non-ribawi. If both sides contain ribawi items of the same genus, special care is needed.
Riba control is the key factor.
2
Check if items are uniform or variable
For non-riba sales, if the items on both sides are of the same type and similar (e.g., wheat for wheat of same quantity), division is by parts (each part equals one unit). If they vary (e.g., cow for sheep), division is by market value.
Uniformity is about the type, not necessarily exact equality.
3
Apply riba-validating division
For riba sales, the division must be done in a way that avoids riba. Typically, same genus items must offset each other equally, and any excess is matched with a different genus. The example: 10 dirhams for 5 dirhams and a dinar — the 5 dirhams cancel 5 dirhams, the remaining 5 dirhams are matched with the dinar (different genus).
This ensures that no unequal exchange of same genus occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الإيضاح الأصل في هذا الباب أن حقيقة البيع إذا اشتملت على إبدال وجب قسمة أحد البدلين على الآخر، وتظهر الفائدة في الرد بالعيب والرجوع بالثمن عند الاستحقاق ووجوب الشفعة فيما تجب فيه الشفعة، فإن كان العقد مما لا ربا فيه فإن كان مما لا يتفاوت فالقسمة على الأجزاء، وإن كان مما يتفاوت فالقسمة على القيمة. وأما ما فيه الربا فإنما تجب القسمة على الوجه الذي يصح به العقد مثاله : باع عشرة دراهم بخمسة دراهم ودينار يصح العقد فإن الخمسة بالخمسة والخمسة الأخرى بالدينار، وكذا لو قابل جنسين بجنسين كما في مسألة الكتاب اهـ.
In al-Idah: The principle in this chapter is that when a sale involves an exchange of two sets of goods, it is necessary to apportion one of the two considerations to the other. The benefit appears in the case of return due to defect, recovery of price upon right of ownership, and the obligation of pre-emption in those cases where pre-emption is due. If the contract does not involve riba, then if the items do not vary [in value], the division is by parts; and if they vary, the division is by value. As for that which involves riba, division is only required in the manner that validates the contract. Example: If one sells ten dirhams for five dirhams and a dinar, the contract is valid: the five dirhams are for five dirhams, and the other five are for the dinar. Similarly, if one matches two genera with two genera, as in the book's issue. End.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from al-Idah lays out the fundamental rule for dividing consideration in sales that involve multiple items on both sides. The principle applies practically when there is a defect, price recovery, or pre-emption. In non-riba sales, the division is by number of parts if the items are of the same type (e.g., wheat for wheat), but by value if they are of different types (e.g., a cow for a sheep). In riba-prone sales (like gold/silver), the division must be done in a way that validates the contract, i.e., by matching same genus with same genus in equal amounts and allowing the remainder to be matched with a different genus. The example illustrates: ten dirhams can be exchanged for five dirhams and a dinar because the five dirhams offset five dirhams, and the remaining five are offset by the dinar (different genus). This is exactly the same principle as the redirecting genus discussed earlier, now articulated as a general rule for all riba sales.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Division or apportionment of one consideration among multiple items in a sale.
بدل (badal): Consideration; the thing given in exchange (price or commodity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale that involves riba (e.g., gold/silver), how is the consideration divided?
A) By the number of parts regardless of genus
B) By the value of each item
C) In the manner that validates the contract, usually by matching same genus equally
D) The division is not necessary

Key Takeaway
In sales with multiple items, the consideration must be divided correctly: by parts if uniform non-riba, by value if variable non-riba, and by matching same genus equally if riba.
